{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"Lumber prices continue to fall, and are headed to as low as $350 by August, an analyst says","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/lumber-price-today-outlook-august-analyst-commodities-prices-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60deef7a4a93e200191299a8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Lumber prices sawmill US logs wood\" height=\"1990\" width=\"3980\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Lumber prices plummeted in June.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Carolyn Cole/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>An analyst says the price of lumber will sink to as low as $350 by end of August.</li>\n<li>Still, the industry will continue to face headwinds, especially when it comes to labor.</li>\n<li>The price of lumber is trading at $642 per thousand board feet, roughly 62% lower from its May 7 peak.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/commodities/lumber-price?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Lumber</a> futures are sliding after brief pop last week, falling 21% in the last five days as the hot commodity comes down from dizzying highs.</p><p>The price of lumber is trading at $642 per thousand board feet, roughly 62% lower from its May 7 peak of $1,670 per thousand board feet.</p><p>But the downtrend after scaling to unprecedented highs should be expected, said Troy Merkel, partner and senior real estate analyst at Chicago-based consulting firm RSM. He said he expects the price of the commodity to moderate, especially as supply chains normalize and recover after the last year of the pandemic. </p><p>By the end of August and into early September, he told Insider the price of lumber may settle between $350-$450 per thousand board feet due to a confluence of factors, including sawmills slowly reopening and vaccination rates rising.</p><p>And while Merkel still sees headwinds for the industry, especially when it comes to labor, he said he is optimistic the market will normalize by the end of the year. </p><p>Experts, including Merkel, have long sounded the alarm of a chronic shortage of affordable and available homes in the US.</p><p>&#34;People took for granted the prices of lumber,&#34; Merkel told Insider.</p><p>The spike in the price of lumber on its own has added $36,000 to the average price of a new home, according to the National Association of Home Builders<strong>.</strong></p><p>A <a href=\"https://cdn.nar.realtor/sites/default/files/documents/Housing-is-Critical-Infrastructure-Social-and-Economic-Benefits-of-Building-More-Housing-6-15-2021.pdf\">June 2021 report</a> by the Rosen Consulting Group, a real estate economics consulting firm, found that more than two million housing units need to be built per year in the next decade in order to fill an underbuilding gap of at least 5.5 million housing units.</p><p>Homebuilding would need to accelerate to a pace that is well above the current trend, the study said. </p><p>But for some, like David Russell, VP of market intelligence at TradeStation Group, an online broker-dealer, the whole market &#34;distortion&#34; of lumber was an aberration caused by the pandemic.</p><p>&#34;I think in some ways lumber is really just toilet paper, 2.0. It&#39;s just a symptom of a totally weird situation that has almost never happened in history,&#34; he told Insider. &#34;This recession was caused by something totally external.&#34;</p><p>Russell said prices will normalize by the end of the year, though he does not think they will return to pre-pandemic level.</p><p>&#34;The likelihood of this happening again is very low,&#34; he said. &#34;This happened exactly because no one thought it was going to happen.&#34;</p><p>A number of commodities have surged in part because of distorted supply chains during the pandemic, but lumber in particular has captured people&#39;s attention. When asked why people have been focused on lumber over other commodities, Merkel said: &#34;At the end of the day, people need a place to live. Housing has a personal feel, whether you&#39;re an analyst or a prospective homebuyer.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a without.</p><p>According to new <a href=\"https://sensortower.com/blog/tiktok-downloads-3-billion\">Sensor Tower</a> data, TikTok is the fifth non-game app to ever surpass the three billion install mark. The only other apps to have gathered more than three billion downloads since January 2014 are Facebook and its WhatsApp, Messenger, and Instagram.</p><p>Facebook, however, still has more monthly active users around the globe - <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tiktok-pitch-deck-shows-new-e-commerce-ads-2021-4?r=US&IR=T#the-decks-tout-its-audience-more-than-100-million-monthly-active-users-in-the-us-and-732-million-globally-2ly-2\">TikTok&#39;s reported 732 million MAUs</a> fall short of Facebook&#39;s <a href=\"https://www.statista.com/statistics/346167/facebook-global-dau/#:~:text=With%20roughly%202.85%20billion%20monthly,most%20popular%20social%20network%20worldwide.\">2.85 billion.</a></p><p>The popular video-sharing TikTok app has soared in popularity since it launched in 2016, breeding a new enclave of social media influencers and its unique brand of digital culture. <a href=\"https://www.emarketer.com/content/tiktok-users-around-world-2020?_ga=2.243176962.105253583.1626095541-560053885.1585103046\">People really started using the app more</a> during the pandemic as many sought entertainment while shut inside their homes.</p><p>Its success has even prompted its competitors to come out with their own TikTok-like features. <a for users that now appears in the app&#39;s Feed and Explore pages.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"The chief talent officer of enterprise tech company HPE shares her 3 best pieces of career advice for breaking into in-demand industries","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/hewlett-packard-enterprise-chief-talent-officer-career-advice-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60a50d3cf27b4c0019445453?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Black young businesswoman listening to discussion of lawyers during meeting at office\" height=\"2272\" width=\"3030\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Maskot/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Alessandra Ginante Yockelson is chief talent officer at fintech company Hewlett Packard Enterprise.</li>\n<li>She said any aspiring professional can achieve their career goals with the right approach.</li>\n<li>Build your professional and personal confidence and champion diversity at every stage, she said.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Each year, more than half of a million professionals apply to job vacancies at Hewlett Packard Enterprise, a fintech company based in Houston, Texas. Only 12,000 of these applicants were hired globally in 2019.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60e88d6061b8600019f165c7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Alessandra Ginante Yockelson\" height=\"300\" width=\"400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Alessandra Ginante Yockelson.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Alessandra Ginante Yockelson</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Despite the seemingly low odds of landing a position with this enterprise tech leader, HPE&#39;s chief talent officer Alessandra Ginante Yockelson said that nearly 40% of hires in 2019 were gender diverse.</p><p>As a woman and immigrant, Yockelson understands that each professional faces unique intersectionalities. She believes that any aspiring professional has the ability to achieve their career goals even if they&#39;re confronted with societal barriers.</p><p>&#34;I come from a very humble family in São Paulo, Brazil,&#34; Yockelson told Insider. &#34;I had to overcome a lot of adversities in the beginning.&#34;</p><p>She advises job seekers in every industry to follow these three pieces of advice.</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">1. Build your confidence professionally and personally</strong></h2><p>&#34;Believe that no matter where you start from - no matter how limited your resources are or how victimized you are by institutionalized racism - there&#39;s a way forward and a strength in you that will show,&#34; Yockelson said.</p><p>Experts suggest that low levels of confidence <a href=\"https://www.foxbusiness.com/features/how-confidence-affects-employment-and-the-job-hunt\">negatively impact your career</a>, especially if you&#39;re a recent graduate.</p><p>To build confidence as a person and professional, consider first embracing your past accomplishments, identifying your weaknesses, and strengthening your resume. Other suggestions include:</p><ul><li aria-level=\"1\">Learning how to align the skill set, achievements, and knowledge you&#39;ve already developed with the requirements of the role you seek</li><li aria-level=\"1\">Highlighting the skills or certifications that you lack and identifying ways to formally improve them</li><li aria-level=\"1\">Continuing to enhance your resume through freelance projects and volunteering</li><li aria-level=\"1\">Seeking out support from peers to help you remain on-track to achieving your goals</li><li aria-level=\"1\">When feeling lost, consider taking aptitude tests to help you refocus on your unique motivational drivers, expositional traits, and learning style</li></ul><h2><strong>2. Utilize free resources</strong></h2><p>Yockelson recently earned her doctorate in business administration. &#34;Education, I truly believe in my case, has opened doors,&#34; she said.</p><p>The pandemic has expanded online opportunities and free resources. Princeton, Harvard, and Yale are among the many universities that offer <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/free-online-courses-from-best-colleges#1-princeton-university-1\">online courses through edX and Coursera</a>, which also features courses led by companies like Google Cloud.</p><p>Yockelson insists that job seekers keep in mind that academia isn&#39;t the sole provider of education. She encourages everyone to seek out diverse experiences outside of their comfort zones, even if that means simply grabbing lunch with people you don&#39;t know at work.</p><h2><strong style=\"color: #000000;\">3. Proactively champion diversity at every stage</strong></h2><p>Regardless of industry, all professionals have the power to champion diversity at every stage of their careers.</p><p>Leaders can <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-build-diverse-inclusive-workforce-small-business-2020-10\">immediately increase diversity on their teams</a> by expanding the scope of job requirements, standardizing the interview process, and intentionally sponsoring employees belonging to minority groups.</p><p>By purposefully and publicly making an effort to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-employers-can-use-pandemic-to-create-diverse-inclusive-workplace-2020-5\">counter the &#34;invisibility effect,&#34;</a> leaders can elevate their existing employees while encouraging other diverse candidates in the workforce to pursue these roles.</p><p>Achieving certain career goals may seem impossible for those affected by intersectionality in the workplace, but Yockelson is determined to give these diverse professionals hope.</p><p>&#34;If they knew my story, they would believe that they could do it as well,&#34; she said.</p><div 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"It's starting to look like Republicans aren't going support the bipartisan infrastructure deal","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/republicans-biden-infrastructure-deal-congress-white-house-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eeee10a8d8c00019b03152?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mitch McConnell senate republicans\" height=\"2007\" width=\"4014\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Senate Minority Leader Mitch McConnell speaks at a press conference alongside Senate Republicans.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Alex Wong/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>It appears that Republicans won&#39;t ultimately support the bipartisan infrastructure deal. </li>\n<li>At least two GOP senators who signed on are criticizing an ensuing Democrat-only spending bill that will move alongside it.</li>\n<li>Mitch McConnell hasn&#39;t said whether he backs the $579 billion agreement.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Senate Republicans are mostly keeping their cards close to the vest when it comes to the $579 billion bipartisan infrastructure agreement. </p><p>Senate Minority Leader Mitch McConnell hasn&#39;t thrown his support behind the package yet, even though it was negotiated by a handful of Senate Republicans that included Mitt Romney if Utah and Susan Collins of Maine. The framework is concentrated on physical items like roads and bridges. It also contains funding for broadband internet, a major priority for both parties.</p><p>There doesn&#39;t appear to be a lot of enthusiasm among Republicans to back the agreement yet, which could partly stem from the fact that negotiators are still turning the blueprint into a formal bill. Democrats are pressing to finalize the details this week, but Republicans say a bill won&#39;t be ready until next week.</p><p>A total of 11 GOP senators signed onto the bipartisan agreement, which would be enough for the plan to clear the 60-vote threshold if every Democratic senator voted for it as well.</p><p>But some have signaled they could withdraw their support given that Democrats are poised to advance a separate $3.5 trillion party-line package through reconciliation in the coming weeks. That legislative pathway requires Democrats to stick together in an evenly-divided Senate over united Republican opposition - and both measures would be approved on parallel tracks.</p><p>&#39;This deal is troublesome to me,&#34; said Sen. Jerry Moran of Kansas, a GOP sponsor, on Wednesday.</p><p>Others say they don&#39;t want the bipartisan deal&#39;s fate to be tied to the Democrat-only plan. House Speaker Nancy Pelosi has insisted the House will only approve a bipartisan bill once the Senate clears a party-line infrastructure bill. &#34;They certainly can&#39;t be connected,&#34; Sen. Lindsay Graham, another Republican sponsor, told reporters on Wednesday.</p><p>Republicans have also started criticizing the funding mechanisms, potentially making it harder for more Republicans to support an agreement.</p><p>Some experts <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-republican-bipartisan-infrastructure-plan-paid-for-pixie-dust-2021-6\">are skeptical</a> that the funding provisions of the bipartisan deal - which include repurposing coronavirus relief funds and unspent federal unemployment aid - will fully pay for itself. Howard Gleckman, a tax expert at the nonpartisan Tax Policy Center, called it &#34;pixie dust&#34; <a href=\"https://www.taxpolicycenter.org/taxvox/paying-infrastructure-pixie-dust\">in a recent blog post.</a></p><p>The GOP is seizing on that given their opposition to growing the national debt. Sen. John Cornyn of Texas said in a Tuesday interview that Republicans want &#34;just to make sure the pay-fors are responsible, actually real and not illusory,&#34; he said.</p><p>Sen. John Thune, the second-ranked Senate Republican, told reporters on Tuesday that a plan that&#39;s fully paid for would be a &#34;prerequisite for a lot of Republicans to support it.&#34;</p><p>A day later, Thune said that <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/senate-democrats-reach-deal-reconciliation-package-2021-7\">the $3.5 trillion spending deal</a> could &#34;put downward pressure on Republican votes&#34; in the weeks ahead.</p><p>&#34;I don&#39;t think it helps. We have members who truly do want to get an infrastructure bill,&#34; he said.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Security and Defense Department.</p><p>Taliban militants are making gains across the country as US forces pullout, sparking fears they will torture or kill fellow Afghans who translated for US forces, worked on their bases or otherwise assisted the NATO coalition.</p><p>Potentially tens of thousands of Afghans are seeking special immigrant visas to go to the US, with categories for those who worked as translators or interpreters as well as those generally employed by the US or on its behalf. Interpreters took on heightened risks by accompanying NATO troops on missions and using their knowledge of local customs and languages like Dari and Pashto to assist them.</p><p>Former President George W. 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"George W. Bush participates in a video teleconference with Afghanistan Provincial Reconstruction Team Leaders and Brigade Combat Commanders at the White House in Washington, DC, on March 13, 2008.\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Then-President George W. Bush participates in a video teleconference with Afghanistan Provincial Reconstruction Team Leaders and Brigade Combat Commanders at the White House in Washington, DC, on March 13, 2008.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Jim Watson/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>George W. Bush ripped into Joe Biden&#39;s withdrawal of US troops from Afghanistan. </li>\n<li>Bush warned the pullout endangered women, girls, and people who worked with foreign troops.</li>\n<li>&#34;They&#39;re just going to be left behind to be slaughtered by these very brutal people, and it breaks my heart.&#34;</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Almost twenty years after ordering troops into Afghanistan, former President George W. Bush criticized President Joe Biden&#39;s order to withdraw remaining personnel as endangering women, girls and those who&#39;d supported the US and the Afghan central government.</p><p>Bush during <a href=\"https://www.dw.com/en/george-w-bush-afghanistan-troop-withdrawal-a-mistake/a-58261709\">an interview with German broadcaster Deutsche Welle</a> warned that the consequences of withdrawing US and NATO troops from Afghanistan will be &#34;unbelievably bad.&#34;</p><p>&#34;I&#39;m afraid Afghan women and girls are going to suffer unspeakable harm,&#34; Bush said, characterizing the pullout as a mistake without saying how he would quell the violence or when US troops should leave the longest war in its history.</p><p>The former president, who has largely refrained from making political remarks since leaving office, also expressed concern about Afghans who worked as translators or offered other support to foreign troops. &#34;They&#39;re just going to be left behind to be slaughtered by these very brutal people, and it breaks my heart,&#34; Bush said.</p><p>Bush said he believed German Chancellor Angela Merkel &#34;feels the same way.&#34;</p><p>The war in Afghanistan, part of the broader &#34;war on terror,&#34; began under Bush. The US invaded Afghanistan in October 2001, not long after the 9/11 terror attacks that were carried out by extremists, mostly from Saudi Arabia, acting on the orders of al Qaeda leaders like Osama bin Laden thought to be based in Afghanistan. Roughly two decades later, the US is ending its military operations but the war on terror rages on.</p><p>The &#34;global war on terror&#34; that was launched by the Bush administration has killed over 800,000 people in direct war violence and led to the displacement of at least 37 million, according to a report from Brown University&#39;s Costs of War project. The federal government also places the cost of the war on terror at <a href=\"https://watson.brown.edu/costsofwar/\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\" data-uri=\"d63308060dc9c818adeaa8876dd29711\">over $6.4 trillion.</a>  </p><p>The war on terror remains among the most controversial aspects of Bush&#39;s legacy, and scholars have widely characterized it as <a href=\"https://www.cato.org/policy-analysis/step-back-lessons-us-foreign-policy-failed-war-terror\">a major failure</a> that <a href=\"https://www.foreignaffairs.com/articles/afghanistan/2020-10-22/us-foreign-policy-never-recovered-war-terror#author-info\">damaged US credibility</a> around the world.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5f57eed1e6ff30001d4e79df?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mission Accomplished\" height=\"1125\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Bush delivering a speech to crew aboard the aircraft carrier USS Abraham Lincoln, as the carrier steamed toward San Diego, California on May 1, 2003.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Larry Downing/Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h2>Biden continues to defend the Afghanistan withdrawal as the Taliban makes gains</h2><p>The human and economic cost of the conflict is a large part of the reason Biden, who as a senator voted in favor of the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-backs-congress-post-911-laws-led-to-forever-wars-2021-3\">laws that paved the way for war on terror</a>, has moved to end US involvement in Afghanistan.</p><p>Proponents of the withdrawal say it&#39;s long overdue, and that the US has already lost too many lives and resources in the country. Opponents of the pullout say it&#39;s too hasty and will effectively hand the country to militants on a silver platter. The Taliban recently said it&#39;s taken over <a href=\"https://apnews.com/article/joe-biden-europe-middle-east-afghanistan-taliban-c119addda2138516b40d42567e5742cd\">85% of the country&#39;s territory,</a> though it&#39;s difficult to verify this. <a href=\"https://www.longwarjournal.org/archives/2021/07/afghanistan-at-risk-of-collapse-as-taliban-storms-the-north.php\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" aria-label=\"according to The Foundation for Defense of Democracies (opens in a new window)\">According to The Foundation for Defense of Democracies,</a> the Taliban currently controls 195 of the country&#39;s 407 districts and is contesting another 129.</p><p>There are serious concerns about the ability of the Afghan military to maintain control of the country and prevent the Taliban from taking over. Almost as soon as US troops in early July departed from Bagram, the largest air base in the country, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/looters-ransacked-bagram-airbase-afghanistan-as-soon-as-us-left-2021-7\">it was ransacked by looters</a>. Control of the airbase was transferred over to the Afghan military, but local officials claimed the US did not coordinate with them and left in the dead of the night. </p><p>Earlier this week, CNN released video footage of <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/video-shows-taliban-executing-22-afghan-commandos-cnn-2021-7\">22 Afghan commandos being executed</a> by the Taliban as they attempted to surrender. Responding to this report, GOP Rep. Adam Kinzinger, a US Air Force veteran who flew missions in Afghanistan, tweeted, &#34;This is horrible - yet it&#39;s the reality of announcing the U.S. withdrawal from Afghanistan. Removing the peacekeepers and leaving the Afghan people without support is a grave mistake, Mr. President.&#34;</p><p>Meanwhile, the Taliban continues to make gains as local militias pop up to challenge it, propelling the country further and further into a state of civil war. </p><p>On Friday, Pentagon spokesperson John Kirby acknowledged the <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2021/07/09/pentagon-warning-taliban-advances-498924\">&#34;deteriorating security situation&#34;</a> in Afghanistan, just one day after Biden gave a full-throated defense of the withdrawal.</p><p>The president announced the pullout in April, and last week said the US military mission in the country would be complete by the end of August. Biden has rejected the notion a Taliban takeover of the country is inevitable in the absence of US troops, expressing confidence in the Afghan military&#39;s capacity to keep the insurgents at bay.</p><p>&#34;We did not go to Afghanistan to nation-build. And it&#39;s the right and the responsibility of the Afghan people alone to decide their future and how they want to run their country,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.whitehouse.gov/briefing-room/speeches-remarks/2021/07/08/remarks-by-president-biden-on-the-drawdown-of-u-s-forces-in-afghanistan/\">Biden said</a> in an impassioned speech. &#34;Nearly 20 years of experience has shown us that the current security situation only confirms that &#39;just one more year&#39; of fighting in Afghanistan is not a solution but a recipe for being there indefinitely.&#34; </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a Chinese tech stocks amid an ongoing regulatory crackdown, according to Ark&#39;s daily trading updates.</p><p>Ark&#39;s flagship <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/etfs/ark-innovation-etf-us00214q1040\">Disruptive Innovation ETF</a> has seen its exposure to Chinese stocks fall to less than 1% from a high of 8% in February, according to <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-07-14/cathie-wood-sells-china-tech-stocks-warning-of-valuation-reset\">data compiled by Bloomberg.</a> Ark&#39;s exposure to Chinese tech stocks is at its lowest level since 2014.</p><p>Over the past week, the thematic investment manager sold three million shares of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/huya-stock\">HUYA</a>, one million shares of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/tctzf-stock\">Tencent</a>, and more than 600,000 shares of <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/jd-stock\">JD.com</a>. </p><p>The move comes amid increased regulatory scrutiny from China of tech giants like <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/didi-stock\">Didi</a> and ByteDance. Less than a week after its IPO, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/didi-app-suspended-china-personal-data-collection-2021-7\">Didi was removed from Chinese app stores</a> over data security concerns. Those same concerns led to TikTok parent <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/tiktok-bytedance-ipo-plans-as-china-tech-companies-security-didi-2021-7\">ByteDance shelving its planned IPO.</a> China has also led a crackdown on tech giants <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/baba-stock\">Alibaba</a>, Ant Group, and Tencent in recent months. </p><p>In a webinar with investors on Tuesday, Wood said, &#34;From a valuation point of view, these stocks have come down and again from a valuation point of view, probably will remain down.&#34;</p><p>The valuation reset is clear in the current price-to-earnings ratio of Chinese tech giants Alibaba, Baidu, and JD.com.</p><p>According to data from FactSet, Alibaba&#39;s current P/E ratio of 19x is well below its historical P/E ratio of 24x. Baidu&#39;s current P/E of 16x is below its historical P/E of 21x, and JD.com has seen its valuation chopped nearly in half, with its current P/E of 36x below its historical P/E of 62x.</p><p>Since their peak in February, Chinese tech stocks have lost more than $500 billion in market value. </p><p>&#34;I do think there&#39;s a valuation reset,&#34; Wood said on the Tuesday webinar. href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/bitcoin-price-today-inflation-hedge-consumer-price-index-cpi-btc-2021-7\">pace</a> since 2008, according to data on Tuesday. </p><p>Bitcoin Earlier, it fell to as little as $31,599, its lowest in three weeks.</p><p>&#34;The strange narrative is that this is due to the strong inflation yesterday in the US, perhaps on the fear that this will bring forward Fed tightening measures although, we do also have the ongoing backdrop of a Chinese <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/china-crypto-crackdown-regulation-software-firm-central-bank-cryptocurrency-laws-2021-7\">crackdown</a> on mining,&#34; Saxo Bank chief investment officer Steen Jakobsen said.</p><p>Fed fund futures, which track short-term interest rate expectations, suggested traders are betting on the Fed raising interest rates by late 2022, if inflation persists, <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/business/finance/us-fed-funds-futures-up-rate-hike-bets-after-cpi-data-2021-07-13/\">Reuters</a> reported. </p><p>This could affect cryptocurrencies, which have profited from over a year of ultra-cheap money that has sent investors searching high and low for anything that carries a decent yield.</p><p>China&#39;s recent crackdown on crypto <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/china-crypto-crackdown-regulation-software-firm-central-bank-cryptocurrency-laws-2021-7\">trading</a> and the regulatory woes of the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/currencies/news/binance-uk-crypto-clients-stop-from-withdrawing-pounds-again-2021-7\">Binance</a> exchange in various counties - and most recently the United Kingdom on Wednesday - have also contributed to the steady decline in the value of bitcoin and other coins in the past couple of months. </p><p>Bitcoin is still up by about 260% over the last 12 months, but it has fallen by more than 50% since peaking at a record of almost $65,000 in April.</p><p>The trend has been similar in other cryptocurrencies. href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/tucker-carlson/2021/07/13/398fa720-dd9f-11eb-a501-0e69b5d012e5_story.html\">the teacher told the Washington Post. </a></p><p>In <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/gp/product/1501183664?ie=UTF8&tag=thewaspos09-20&camp=1789&linkCode=xm2&creativeASIN=1501183664eASIN=1501183664\">the book, &#34;Ship of Fools,&#34;</a> Carlson described his time in Mrs. Raymond&#39;s first-grade classroom as a kind of conservative awakening that cemented his belief that liberals should &#34;stop blubbering and teach us to read.&#34; </p><p>Carlson, who was in first grade in the 1970s, wrote that Mrs. Raymond, his first-grade teacher at the upscale La Jolla Country Day School in southern California, &#34;wore long Indian-print skirts,&#34; &#34;had little interest in conventional academic topics, like reading and penmanship,&#34; and at one point wailed to students: &#34;The world is so unfair! You don&#39;t know that yet. But you&#39;ll find out!&#34;</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong></em><em><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/republican-women-candidates-to-watch-2022-midterms-house-senate-governor-2021-7\" data-analytics-position=\"10\" data-analytics-module=\"\">11 Republican women to watch in 2022 as the GOP tries to elect more female candidates and close an enormous gender gap</a></em></p><p>He also charged that &#34;Mrs. Raymond never did teach us; my father had to hire a tutor to get me through phonics.&#34;</p><p>The teacher herself, Marianna Raymond, told the Post that none of Carlson&#39;s version of events was true: she didn&#39;t preach social justice, cry in class, or even wear Indian-print skirts. She said she both taught Carlson and, in fact, tutored him outside of school as well, remembering him as &#34;precious&#34; and &#34;very, very polite and sweet&#34; as a child. </p><p>&#34;Oh my God,&#34; Raymond said of Carlson&#39;s description of her as a raging liberal hippie who cried in front of students. &#34;That is the most embellished, crazy thing I ever heard.&#34;</p><p>Raymond said wasn&#39;t even aware that Carlson had characterized her that way until she was interviewed by the Post <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/tucker-carlson/2021/07/13/398fa720-dd9f-11eb-a501-0e69b5d012e5_story.html\">for an extensive profile on Carlson published Wednesday</a> that traces his ascent to a top purveyor of white grievance and racial resentment from his perch hosting the coveted 8 p.m. slot on Fox News, with a contract reportedly <a href=\"https://www.cnn.com/2020/08/27/media/fox-news-pays-10m-tucker-carlson/index.html\">worth</a> $10 million a year.</p><p>Carlson himself was not interviewed for the Post story but told the outlet: &#34;You want to make me shut up, so you call me a racist. any investigation of the company and has accused her of bias, citing her past criticisms of the tech industry.</p><p>Facebook filed a <a Facebook had monopoly power in the online market. The FTC is now deliberating about filing a new lawsuit against the company.</p><p>Facebook&#39;s request to have Khan removed from any deliberations involving the company comes <a investigation at the FTC. </p><p>Amazon argued in June that &#34;Chair Khan&#39;s body of work and public statements demonstrate that she has prejudged the outcome of matters the FTC may examine during her term and, under established law, preclude her from participating in such matters.&#34;</p><p>President Joe Biden appointed Khan to FTC Chair in June, and her extensive background in antitrust law paired with her new role <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/ftc-chair-lina-khan-antitrust-critic-big-tech-amazon-2021-6\">has made waves in the tech and antitrust worlds.</a> Khan 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"Here's what would happen if all the ice on Earth melted overnight","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-if-all-ice-earth-melted-overnight-2019-10","description":"<div style=\"position:relative; overflow:hidden; padding-bottom:56.25%\">\n<iframe src=\"https://cdn.jwplayer.com/players/kjyxjHl8-jZbcmOYf.html\" width=\"100%\" height=\"100%\" style=\"position:absolute;\" allow=\"fullscreen\"></iframe>\n</div><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>If all the ice on Earth melted overnight, the planet would be sent into chaos.</li>\n<li><strong>There would be mass flooding from sea levels rising, severe weather changes, deadly chemical releases, and mass greenhouse gasses that would leak into the atmosphere. </strong></li>\n<li>Scientists say we need to stop the planet from rising in temperature by just 1° Celsius, or this could happen sooner than we think.</li>\n<li>\n<p><strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit Business Insider&#39;s homepage for more stories.</a></strong></p>\n</li>\n</ul><p><em>Following is a transcript of the video.</em></p><p><strong>Narrator: </strong>Ninety-nine percent of all freshwater ice on Earth is sitting on top of Greenland and Antarctica, and each year, a little more of it melts into the ocean. Normally, it would take hundreds to thousands of years for it all to melt away. But what if something happened that caused a massive global melt overnight?</p><p>As we slept, sea levels would rise by a whopping 66 meters. Coastal cities like New York, Shanghai, and London would drown in the apocalyptic mass flood, forcing up to 40% of the world&#39;s population out of their homes. While all this chaos ensues aboveground, something equally sinister is happening below. All that rising saltwater will infiltrate groundwater reserves farther inland, forcing its way into nearby freshwater aquifers. You know, the ones that supply our drinking water, irrigation systems, and power-plant cooling systems? All those aquifers would be destroyed. Not good.</p><p>On top of that, the ice on Greenland and Antarctica is made of freshwater, so when it melts, that&#39;s about 69% of the world&#39;s freshwater supply that&#39;s going straight into the oceans. This will wreak havoc on our ocean currents and weather patterns. Take the Gulf Stream, for example. It&#39;s a strong ocean current that brings warm air to northern Europe and relies on dense, salty water from the Arctic in order to function. But a flood of freshwater would dilute the current and could weaken or even stop it altogether. Without that warm air, temperatures in northern Europe would plummet, and that could spawn a mini ice age, according to some experts.</p><p>That&#39;s not even the worst of it. Take a look at what will happen when that last 1% of freshwater ice that&#39;s not part of Greenland or Antarctica thaws. Some of that 1% is sitting in glaciers farther inland. The Himalayan glaciers specifically pose one of the largest threats because of what&#39;s trapped inside: toxic chemicals like dichlorodiphenyltrichloroethane, or DDT. Scientists discovered that glaciers like this can store these chemicals for decades. But as they thaw, those glaciers release the chemicals into rivers, lakes, and groundwater reserves, poisoning each one as they go.</p><p>The rest of that 1% is hanging out underground, mostly in the Arctic tundra, as something called permafrost. Permafrost is organic matter that&#39;s been frozen in the ground for two-plus years. Now, one of the most immediate problems with thawing permafrost would be mercury poisoning. That&#39;s right: There are an estimated 15 million gallons of mercury stored up in the Arctic permafrost. That&#39;s almost equal to the amount of mercury everywhere else on Earth. On top of that, the organic matter in permafrost is a tasty meal for microorganisms. After they digest it all, they fart out two of the most potent greenhouse gases out there, carbon dioxide and methane. Scientists estimate this could double the current levels of greenhouse gases in the atmosphere, and potentially cause global temperatures to rise by 3.5 degrees Celsius compared to today.</p><p>That might not sound like much, but say goodbye to that mini European ice age, and even rivers and lakes around the world. They&#39;d evaporate from the higher temperatures and cause mass droughts and desert-like climates. And all that extra water vapor in the atmosphere would fuel more frequent and stronger storms, floods, and hurricanes. So all of that newly established coastline on the eastern US would be one of the last places you&#39;d want to live. Instead, there would be mass migrations to Canada, Alaska, the Arctic, and even what&#39;s left of the Antarctic.</p><p>And you&#39;re right, this is probably never going to happen. After all, there&#39;s enough ice right now to cover the entire continent of North America in a sheet a mile thick. So the next time you hear about record-breaking heat or ultra-powerful hurricanes, at least you know that it could be worse. But scientists estimate that if we don&#39;t take action and global temperatures increase by just 1 degree Celsius, the effects of climate change we already see today will be irreversible. So yes, it could be worse, and it will be if we&#39;re not careful.</p><p><em>EDITOR&#39;S NOTE: This video was originally published in September 2019.</em></p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the Tucker Carlson called former President Donald Trump, then a real-estate mogul toying with a presidential bid, the &#34;most repulsive person on the planet&#34; and &#34;so horrible&#34; in a 1999 post on the website Slate. </p><p>Carlson, then an early-career conservative writer and commentator, made the judgment in an exchange with fellow Slate blogger, Evan Smith, who <a href=\"https://slate.com/human-interest/1999/11/is-drudge-done.html\">first</a> labelled Trump a &#34;repulsive&#34; character.</p><p>&#34;I&#39;d love to add something even meaner to your description of Donald Trump - he&#39;s the sort of person I want to keep kicking once he&#39;s down-but I don&#39;t think I can,&#34; <a repulsive person on the planet.&#34;</p><p>But Carlson acknowledged that Trump, who was considering a 2000 run as a Reform Party candidate, was more &#34;interesting&#34; than many others in politics. </p><p>&#34;That said, I still plan to write about him some time. I don&#39;t think I&#39;ll be able to help it. His Fox News primetime show, &#34;Tucker Carlson Tonight,&#34; debuted shortly after Trump&#39;s election in 2016 and has become the most-watched cable news show in the country. </p><p>Fox News offense and can receive a fine or be sentenced to imprisonment for a period not exceeding three years,&#34; Cele said, citing a law known as The Cybersecurity Act, which he said prohibits people in South Africa from using the internet to incite violence or encourage the destruction of private property. </p><p>&#34;As the cluster, we are monitoring all social media platforms and we are tracking </p><p>&#34;Our business is taking a firearm of known value and transforming it into a personalized invaluable treasure for a fair price,&#34; the company said in a <a It is our business to assist firearms owners in making their guns better reflect them as a person and individual, our pieces speak to the owner of the gun as they have selected those options from a seemingly infinite range of possibilities.&#34;</p><p>The company also said it wants the Block19 to represent &#34;the pure enjoyment of the shooting sports.&#34; Culper Precision went on to say covering the gun in <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/lego-has-unveiled-prototype-brick-made-from-recycled-plastic-bottles-2021-6\">LEGOs</a> was an attempt at &#34;making the 2nd amendment too painful to tread on.&#34; The company added that it hopes <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/gun-sales-boom-in-pandemic-millennials-buy-guns-2021-5\">guns</a> can be society&#39;s &#34;great unifier.&#34; </p><p>Gun policy is one of the most polarizing topics in US politics. A recent <a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/politics/2021/04/20/amid-a-series-of-mass-shootings-in-the-u-s-gun-policy-remains-deeply-divisive/\">survey</a> from the Pew Research Center found that 81% of Democrats and Democratic-leaning independents say gun laws should be stricter than they currently are, while 20% of Republicans and Republican leaners share this view. </p><p>&#34;Decorating firearms with one of the most popular children&#39;s toys is a recipe for disaster,&#34; Shannon Watts, founder of gun safety group Moms Demand Action, said in a statement to Insider. &#34;We have already seen tragedies happen when unsecured firearms are around children and they don&#39;t look like toys. Too many children&#39;s lives are cut short by unintentional shootings every year - and in the past year we&#39;ve only seen these tragic instances happen more frequently.&#34; </p><p>So far in 2021, there have been at least 174 unintentional shootings by children, leading to 113 injuries and 70 deaths, according to <a href=\"https://everytownresearch.org/maps/notanaccident/\">data from Everytown</a>. Last year, despite the coronavirus pandemic, the US had <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/2020-more-gun-deaths-than-any-year-over-two-decades-2021-3\">a 20-year-high of gun violence deaths</a>, according to data from the Gun Violence Archive. </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a It's the most populous city in Virginia, made up of numerous inland and coastal communities, with the Virginia Beach Oceanfront being the main resort area.</p><p>Studded with marine-themed statues, including the towering bronze figure of Neptune, the 28-foot-wide paved boardwalk draws tourists and locals alike, who come to stroll, bike, roller-blade, and catch live music and festivals at its many seaside stages.&#160;</p><h2>Where are the best places to stay in a Virginia Beach Airbnb?</h2><p>If you want to be in the middle of the action, opt for the Oceanfront, which stretches from 2nd Street to 40th Street and is packed with hotels, restaurants, bars, and entertainment venues on and around the Boardwalk. Most vacation rentals here are condos and the party atmosphere appeals to a younger crowd.&#160;</p><p>If you want a larger house with amenities and a calmer beach experience, look for Airbnbs in Virginia Beach on the northern end, starting in the mid-30s and going up to 90th Street. The farther north you go, the quieter and more residential it gets.</p><p>During the high summer season, trolleys run frequently from the southern end of the Oceanfront to Shore Drive (roughly 83rd Street), so you can easily get to all the nightlife hotspots.&#160;</p><p>Other desirable oceanfront communities for Airbnbs in Virginia Beach include Croatan and Sandbridge to the south, and to the far north, the tranquil Chesapeake Bay beaches of Chick's Beach offer a truly locals-only experience.</p><h2>What is there to do in Virginia Beach?</h2><p>By far the most popular attraction is the 3-mile-long Virginia Beach Boardwalk, whose wide, paved beachfront path is ideal for strolling, biking, or rollerblading.</p><p>Try your hand at high-octane water sports, including surfing, wakeboarding, parasailing, and jet-skiing, or more relaxing activities like kayaking, stand-up paddleboarding, and fishing.</p><p>State parks offer hiking and biking trails and fantastic bird-watching opportunities. For kids, there's the Virginia Aquarium &#38; Marine Science Center, the Ocean Breeze Waterpark, and several other amusement parks. There's also great dining, with a focus on local seafood, and more than 20 craft breweries and taphouses.</p><h2>How much does it cost to rent a beach house in Virginia Beach?</h2><p>There's a big variety in terms of price, location, size, and amenities. As expected, rentals on or near the beach and close to the buzzy Oceanfront are generally more expensive.</p><p>You can often find better deals on properties along the quieter Chesapeake Bay beaches. &#160; Prices fluctuate wildly depending on the time of year; summer (from Memorial Day through Labor Day) is peak season so expect a surge in prices, especially on weekends and holidays. Shoulder season sees lower rates; September and October, when temps are usually still warm but crowds are fewer, are great months to visit.&#160;</p><p>A two-bedroom bungalow in walking distance to the beach can run as little as $80 per night in October, while that same property in July is $199 per night. Larger properties see bigger price surges, like a five-bedroom oceanside home that can be had for just $250 per night in the off-season, but the summer rate quintuples to $1,250. Many homes book up fast during the coveted summer season so be sure to plan ahead.&#160;</p><p>Be sure to also budget extra fees for cleaning, service fees, and other additional costs imposed by vacation rentals such as Airbnb.</p><h2>Is Virginia Beach open to visitors?</h2><p>If you are planning to travel to Virginia Beach during COVID-19, know that there are no Virginia Beach travel restrictions currently.</p><p>There is a statewide face-covering requirement in place; you can read more about Virginia's current COVID travel restrictions on the <a href=\"https://www.virginia.gov/coronavirus/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">state government's website</a>.&#160;</p><h2>How do I book a vacation rental in Virginia Beach on Airbnb?</h2><p>You may search for homes on Airbnb and filter results based on location, price, date, the number of bedrooms or bathrooms, amenities, and more. For more information on how to book on Airbnb, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnb-vrbo-homeaway#airbnb-booking-processes-cancellation-policies-and-cleanliness-guidelines-2\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">click here</a>.</p><h2>What is Airbnb's cancellation policy?</h2><p>Cancellation policies on Airbnb differ for every home. For a full breakdown of Airbnb's cancellation policies, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/airbnbs-cancellation-policy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">click here</a>.</p><h2>Is it safe to stay in an Airbnb right now?</h2><p>Experts say that&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/are-airbnbs-safe-coronavirus\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">private home rentals on Airbnb are safe</a>, especially <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/which-is-safer-airbnb-hotels-coronavirus\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">compared to hotels</a>. The CDC also now says it's&#160;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/cdc-fully-vaccinated-travelers-can-now-travel-in-the-us-2021-4\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">safe for fully vaccinated individuals to travel domestically in the US</a>.</p><p>However, there are still risks associated with traveling. Be sure to follow CDC guidelines, such as practicing social distancing, wearing a mask, and washing hands frequently.</p>\n\tMore East Coast Airbnb beach homes\n\t<figure>\n\t<img href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/video/2021/07/14/watch-cnbcs-full-interview-with-blackrock-ceo-larry-fink.html\">told CNBC</a> on Wednesday he doesn&#39;t believe the surge in inflation gripping the world will be fleeting, and the way the Federal Reserve and other central banks navigate this environment will have great significance.</p><p>&#34;I do not believe inflation is going to be transitory,&#34; he told CNBC&#39;s &#34;Squawk Box&#34; after <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/consumer-price-index-inflation-june-2021-7?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestgest\" target=\"_blank\" the <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/inflation-outlook-impact-transitory-10-companies-already-passing-costs-consumers-2021-6\">argument that rising prices will indeed be shortages.</p><p>&#34;We are seeing a real disconnect between the countries that have been very vaccinated and moving forward on vaccination, and the countries that have been late in vaccination, but focusing more on isolation,&#34; he said. &#34;Isolation worked before we had a vaccination.&#34;</p><p>That could lead to uneven recovery across the world. But with record amounts of monetary stimulus and cash still waiting to be put to work, the growth trajectory is eventually pointing upward, he said.</p><p>&#34;I believe the trend line is still going to be upward, maybe not as fast, maybe it&#39;s going to be very moderate for the next six months as we digest how the world is able to handle the Delta variant and the speed in which vaccinations occur throughout the world,&#34; he said.</p><p>Fink, who has previously said <a class</a>, said BlackRock is seeing low investor demand for bitcoin.</p><p>&#34;That is just not part of the focus on retirement and long-term investors,&#34; he said about demand for cryptocurrencies. &#34;We see very little in terms of investor demand on those types of things, but quite frankly (many)<strong data-stringify-type=\"bold\"> </strong>may not come to BlackRock for soar","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/south-korea-gyms-ban-fast-music-cap-treadmill-speeds-covid-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60eefabba8d8c00019b031b8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"man on treadmill in South Korean gym\" height=\"3718\" width=\"5400\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>People exercise at a gym in Yeon-Je/AFP via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>South Korea is seeing a spike in coronavirus cases.</li>\n<li>Health officials have asked gym-goers to slow down in attempt to curb the spread.</li>\n<li>Some experts are skeptical that capping music and treadmill speeds will be effective.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>South Korea is tightening coronavirus prevention measures as the country sees <a href=\"https://www.reuters.com/world/asia-pacific/south-korea-raise-covid-19-curbs-highest-level-seoul-says-pm-2021-07-08/\">record-breaking daily case rates</a>. Although Seoul is not yet going into full lockdown, residents are not allowed to go to nightclubs or large social gatherings for at least two weeks.</p><p>They&#39;re also not permitted to work out hard and fast at the gym. Under the new regulations, treadmills are capped at 3.7 miles per hour, and music played over the gym speakers cannot exceed 120 beats per minute. </p><p>For reference, that&#39;s about the tempo of &#34;<a href=\"https://songbpm.com/@carly-rae-jepsen/call-me-maybe-48176c90-5933-4dc5-935d-35cac81a4ddc\">Call Me Maybe&#34;</a> by Carly Rae Jepsen, or the BTS hit <a href=\"https://songbpm.com/@bts/boy-with-luv-with-halsey\">&#34;Boy With Luv.&#34;</a> Both songs would set the pace for a brisk walk or a really slow jog.</p><p>Dua Lipa&#39;s <a href=\"https://songbpm.com/@dua-lipa/levitating-feat-dababy\">&#34;Levitating&#34;</a> also passes the test at 109 BPM, as does <a href=\"https://tunebat.com/Info/MONTERO-Call-Me-By-Your-Name-Lil-Nas-X/3BZEcbdtXQSo7OrvKRJ6mb\">&#34;MONTERO (Call Me By Your Name)&#34;</a> by Lil Nas X, which clocks in around 89 BPM.</p><p>But anything more strenuous than a power walk has been deemed a transmission risk. (That means gym-goers will not be able to angry run to <a href=\"https://songbpm.com/@olivia-rodrigo/good-4-u-PO84G4NqLk\">&#34;good 4 u&#34;</a> by Olivia Rodrigo or bench press to the beat of Kanye West&#39;s <a href=\"https://songbpm.com/@kanye-west/power\">&#34;Power.&#34;</a>)</p><p>Under the new rules, exercisers are also required to wear masks, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/delta-variant-who-fully-vaccinated-wear-masks-2021-6\">even if fully vaccinated</a>, and workout <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/ways-gyms-can-lower-covid-19-risk-ventilation-expert-2020-11\">class sizes are limited</a>. While those policies could help curb the spread of COVID-19, experts are skeptical that slowing down the music will have the intended effect.</p><h2><strong>Some infectious disease experts are baffled by the new rule</strong></h2><p>The goal of the new gym restrictions is to prevent heavy breathing and sweating on other gym-goers, <a href=\"http://www.koreaherald.com/view.php?ud=20210712000804\">according to health officials</a>.</p><p>&#34;When you run faster, you spit out more respiratory droplets, so that&#39;s why we are trying to restrict heavy cardio exercises,&#34; Son Young-rae, spokesperson for the Ministry of Health and Welfare, <a href=\"http://www.koreaherald.com/view.php?ud=20210712000804\">said in a radio interview Monday</a>.</p><p>But some scientists and lawmakers aren&#39;t buying it.</p><p>Dr. Kim Woo-joo, an infectious disease specialist at Korea University Guro Hospital in Seoul, told the <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/07/13/world/asia/south-korea-gyms-covid.html?campaign_id=154&#38;emc=edit_cb_20210713&#38;instance_id=35224&#38;nl=coronavirus-briefing&#38;regi_id=55940019&#38;segment_id=63339&#38;te=1&#38;user_id=58ac7270b12f323ded9a1c824aac3aa77270b12f323ded9a1c824aac3aa7\">New York Times</a> the gym policies were &#34;absurd&#34; and &#34;ineffective.&#34;</p><p>&#34;So you don&#39;t get COVID-19 if you walk slower than 6 km per hour?&#34; said Kim Yong-tae, a member of the main opposition People Power Party, <a href=\"https://www.nbcnews.com/news/world/south-korea-mandates-slower-gym-music-covid-19-cases-spike-n1273793\">according to Reuters</a>. &#34;And who on earth checks the BPM of the songs when you work out? I don&#39;t understand what COVID-19 has to do with my choice of music.&#34;</p><p>Other experts pointed out that slowing down the music won&#39;t necessarily discourage people from working out at a high intensity. And other prevention measures, like ensuring good ventilation and spacing out gym-goers, have already been <a href=\"https://www.insider.com/how-gym-prevented-outbreak-after-coach-got-covid-19-2020-11\">proven effective</a>.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a While it&#39;s certainly possible to use your phone for taking notes, making video calls, and watching movies, such duties are typically much easier and more enjoyable on a screen larger than six inches.</p><p>But even laptops come with a lot of limitations, especially when serving as the fixture of your home office. Whether you&#39;re looking for add-ons to improve your work-from-home setup or a reliable yet affordable bag for taking your laptop on the go, these are the best laptop accessories you can buy.</p>\n<div id=\"slideshow\">\n\tThe best USB-C hub\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60513c6afe6a340019acf03f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Best USB C Hub Aukey 6 in 1\" height=\"600\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Aukey</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.newegg.com%2Faukey-cb-c75-dvi-hdmi-usb-audio-rj45%2Fp%2F0J2-005J-00014\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Aukey 6-in-1 USB-C Hub Adapter</a></h3><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-cardtype=\"button\" data-pid=\"60512fbe1870630011aa28f4\" data-purchase-option=\"\">6-in-1 USB-C Hub Adapter (button)</bi-shortcode><p>Many of the most portable laptops out there only have a couple of ports, which means it can be challenging to dock your laptop to a monitor and keyboard while still charging it.&#160;</p><p>That's where <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.newegg.com%2Faukey-cb-c75-dvi-hdmi-usb-audio-rj45%2Fp%2F0J2-005J-00014\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Aukey's 6-in-1 USB-C hub</a> comes in. This dock has just about every connection you probably need to turn your laptop into a viable home office computer, including an Ethernet port, an HDMI slot, three USB-3 ports, and a USB-C power delivery port.</p><p>I've been using the 5-in-1 version of this hub for the majority of the past year while working from home, and it's always maintained a quick and reliable connection between my laptop, keyboard, and monitor. Its compact size also means it won't occupy much space at your desk, and it's also easy to stow in your bag if you're carrying your laptop back and forth from the office.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"5b3e60b4447aad1d008b4a83\" data-title=\"The 9 best USB-C hubs of 2021 for connecting more devices to a computer\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-usb-c-hub\" data-thumbnail=\"https://i.insider.com/5ffe0127fe7e140019f7e867\">Related Article Module: The 9 best USB-C hubs of 2021 for connecting more devices to a computer</bi-shortcode><p>However, as our writer Matthew S. Smith points out in our guide to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-usb-c-hub\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">the best USB-C hubs</a>, this dock will likely feel slow when connected to a 4K monitor since it only supports a refresh rate of 30Hz at that resolution. With that in mind, it's best-suited for those using a 1080p monitor.</p>\n\tThe best mouse\n\t<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ec550961b8600019f16949?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Logitech MX Master 3\" height=\"900\" width=\"1200\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Logitech</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure>\n\t<h3><a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B07S395RWD\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Logitech MX Master 3</a></h3><bi-shortcode id=\"commerce-link\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-cardtype=\"button\" data-pid=\"5fa2ec55acfefb499456cc4a\" data-purchase-option=\"\">MX Master 3 (button)</bi-shortcode><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"59303bdab74af4f83d8b55b7\" data-title=\"The best computer mouse of 2021 for gaming, work, and travel\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/best-computer-mouse\" data-thumbnail=\"https://i.insider.com/5e6bc61984159f583f4c7432\">Related Article Module: The best computer mouse of 2021 for gaming, work, and travel</bi-shortcode><p>The <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/dp/B07S395RWD\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Logitech MX Master 3</a> checks all the boxes when it comes to the features that make a great productivity mouse: an ergonomic design, plenty of input options, and customizable shortcuts. 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"23 Democrats are worried about 'plunging' student-loan borrowers back into repayment in October without a long-term plan for protecting their wages and credit scores","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/student-loan-debt-payment-pause-education-department-elizabeth-warren-pressley-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60d9dafe36cf170019de7f9d?format=jpeg\" alt=\"college graduates\" height=\"1335\" width=\"1780\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">Brad Doherty/AP Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>23 Democrats asked the Education Dept. how it will protect borrowers&#39; wages when student-loan payments resume.</li>\n<li>They cited how nearly half of borrowers with defaulted loans can&#39;t return to good credit standing.</li>\n<li>Democrats are worried about &#34;plunging&#34; the borrowers back into repayment in October without long-term help.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>Even if the pause on student-loan payments does get extended past October, it would only be temporary. Lawmakers want to ensure the Education Department has plans for long-term borrower protections.</p><p>On Wednesday, Sen. Elizabeth Warren of Massachusetts, Sen. Cory Booker of New Jersey, and Rep. Ayanna Pressley of Massachusetts led 23 of their Democratic colleagues in requesting information from the Education Department on practices that &#34;harm student borrowers.&#34; Specifically, in their <a href=\"https://www.warren.senate.gov/imo/media/doc/Letter%20to%20ED%20about%20Wage%20Garnishment%20and%20Treasury%20Offset.pdf\">letter</a> to Education Secretary Miguel Cardona, the lawmakers wanted to know the steps the department is taking to protect borrowers&#39; wages and benefits when payments resume.</p><p>&#34;Even before the coronavirus disease 2019 (COVID-19) pandemic, collections on defaulted student loans were catastrophic for borrowers in default, who saw their wages, tax refunds, and even Social Security checks confiscated, in addition to being forced to pay exorbitant fees,&#34; the Democrats wrote.</p><p>The letter cited a <a href=\"https://www.americanprogress.org/issues/education-postsecondary/reports/2017/12/14/444011/student-loan-defaulters/\">report</a> from the Center for American Progress that found 45% of borrowers in default have not found a path to return their loan to good credit standing, which makes housing and job opportunities more difficult to land.</p><p>Democrats added that although the CARES Act initially paused student-loan payments during the pandemic, the Education Department and Treasury Department still &#34;improperly garnished and withheld&#34; over $200 million from about 390,000 borrowers during this time.</p><p>&#34;The Department&#39;s failure to fully implement the collections moratorium raises concerns about how it will handle the upcoming scheduled resumption of collections and payments on October 1, 2021,&#34; the letter said.</p><p>The Education Department also said it would refund any wage or tax refunds collected after the pandemic began, but over 23,000 borrowers who had their wages garnished have yet to receive refunds because the department didn&#39;t have borrowers&#39; correct addresses on file, <a href=\"https://www.studentloanborrowerassistance.org/lawsuit-against-devos-ends-fight-for-defaulted-borrowers-continues/\">according to</a> the National Consumer Law Center, which is why the Democrats are stressing the importance of proper preparation to transition into student-loan repayment.</p><p>Many Democrats who have signed this letter are also calling for the payment pause to be <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/student-loan-debt-payment-pause-extensionelizabeth-warren-chuck-schumer-2021-6\">extended</a> through at least March of next year, given that both borrowers and services have said they are <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/student-loan-companies-debt-payment-pause-extension-elizabeth-warren-2021-7\">not prepared</a> to resume payments in just a few months. </p><p>The lawmakers wrote: &#34;As we near the currently scheduled end of the suspension of payments and collections, we are concerned about plunging borrowers back into an untenable financial situation, causing long-term damage to their credit and financial stability and a sudden unnecessary drag on our recovering economy.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original suggested that the US should explore the option of air strikes against Cuba.</p><p>&#34;What should be contemplated right now is a coalition of potential military action in Cuba,&#34; Suarez, a Republican, said in comments on Fox News. Suarez, whose father was born in Cuba and was formerly mayor of Miami, pointed to US interventions in Panama and Kosovo as potential models to follow. </p><p>When asked if he was calling for air strikes in Cuba, Suarez said, &#34;What I&#39;m suggesting is that option is one that has to be explored, and one that cannot be just simply discarded.&#34;</p><p>Between the disastrous Bay of Pigs invasion and CIA-supported assassination attempts on Fidel Castro, the US has a poor track record when it comes to mounting successful military or covert operations against Cuba&#39;s Communist government.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Andrew Lawrence  (@ndrew_lawrence) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1415033163190095880?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 13, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Suarez&#39;s remarks came after Cuba on Sunday saw the largest anti-government protests in years, with thousands demonstrating against a lack of freedoms and a growing economic crisis under Cuban President Miguel Diaz-Canel and the Communist regime. South Florida has the largest population of Cuban Americans in the country, and Miami in recent days <a href=\"https://abcnews.go.com/US/wireStory/cubans-miami-talk-boating-island-back-protests-78815958\">has seen demonstrations</a> in solidarity with the anti-government protestors in Cuba.</p><p>President Joe Biden on Monday said the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-praises-historic-anti-government-protests-in-cuba-2021-7\">US fully supports the protestors</a>, but his administration is facing pressure on both sides of the aisle to do more.</p><p>While Republicans urge Biden to take a more hardline stance against Cuba&#39;s authoritarian government, a number of Democrats have called on the president to lift the decades-old trade embargo and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/house-democrats-call-on-biden-to-lift-trump-cuba-sanctions-2021-7\">rescind Trump-era sanctions</a> and restrictions that have contributed to medicine and food shortages in the island nation.</p><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Bobby L. Rush  (@RepBobbyRush) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1415333287522934788?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 14, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">-Bernie Sanders  (@SenSanders) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1414785066455158786?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 13, 2021</a></blockquote><script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script><p>Former President Donald Trump reversed the Obama administration&#39;s efforts to open up diplomatic and economic relations with Cuba, tightening the embargo that has been the centerpiece of US policy for six decades. </p><p>Suarez on Tuesday defended the embargo, saying: &#34;I don&#39;t think the embargo is cruel at all. I think the Cuban people aren&#39;t asking for a lifting of the embargo. They&#39;re going out on the streets every single day talking about the failure of the communist regime to provide for its people ... It has failed for six decades.&#34;</p><p>Critics of the US embargo on Cuba contend that it&#39;s failed to foster democratic changes, hurts the Cuban people, and has for years served as a convenient scapegoat for the failings of the Communist government. </p><p>In 2016, then-President Barack Obama called on Congress to lift the embargo.</p><p>&#34;It is an outdated burden on the Cuban people,&#34; <a href=\"https://obamawhitehouse.archives.gov/the-press-office/2016/03/22/remarks-president-obama-people-cuba\">Obama said</a> during a visit to Havana. &#34;It&#39;s a burden on the Americans who want to work and do business or invest here in Cuba. It&#39;s time to lift the embargo.&#34;</p><p>But Biden&#39;s policy toward Cuba so far has been cautious, and has effectively marked a continuing of Trump&#39;s approach to the island nation. Once it gets out of the tube, it&#39;s going to be very hard to put back in.&#34; - <em>quoting Dr. Karl Otto Pohl, the former president of Germany&#39;s Bundesbank, who Gabelli met in the early 1990s.</em></p><p>2. &#34;I find it offensive that somebody can do this on social media.&#34; - <em>criticizing stock promoters and pump-and-dump schemes on Twitter</em>.</p><p>3. &#34;If you drink it - wine, water, beer, soda, whatever - we follow. Anything you watch, anywhere in the world, on any device, and any content or distribution, we cover it. We cluster up our knowledge and try to figure out, &#39;Does this make sense?&#39;&#34; - <em>emphasizing the scale of GAMCO&#39;s industry research.</em></p><p>4. &#34;They think I&#39;m always mad. Let&#39;s stipulate that as a constant.&#34; -<em> commenting on Wall Street&#39;s reaction when he began investing overseas in 1989.</em></p><p>5. &#34;Knock on their door. You can&#39;t do that on a Zoom call. You want to ask a lot of questions. You want to understand how quick the answers are. You want to know how thoughtful they are in terms of handling dynamics of change and handling the simple things. &#39;You&#39;ve got a parts shortage. What are you doing about it? You&#39;ve got a labor shortage. What are you doing about hedging the currency?&#39;&#34; - <em>encouraging investors to speak to companies&#39; management</em>.</p><p>6. &#34;Think of me as a relic of the past, but one that will do quite well over the next 20 years. My window is narrowing but I still have some runway.&#34; - <em>defending his ability to keep performing at age 79</em>.</p><p>7. &#34;The great future is in batteries. When you think about investing over the next 10 to 20 years, we need renewable energy, we need wind, solar, alternative energy, batteries, cybersecurity, and transmission, but the batteries are an important element. The electric vehicles of the world need to have a fast-charging battery with longer mileage as well.&#34;</p><p>8. &#34;I wear hair shirts all my life.&#34; - <em>recalling the opportunities he&#39;s missed including Netflix, which rose 20-fold in value after he decided it was too expensive to buy.</em></p><p>9. &#34;The only time I bought Berkshire Hathaway was in 1985 and we still own it. It was like $3,000 a share.&#34; - <em>Gabelli Funds held 220 of Berkshire&#39;s &#34;A&#34; shares worth $85 million at the end of March.</em></p><p>10. &#34;It would have been nice to sit back and not do any work, retire, go fishing, watch football, and just own Berkshire Hathaway stock. Every so often, if I needed some cash flow, I would take a 1/1500th of a share and sell it. But we would probably get bored, and during certain periods of time, like 1999, the stock did not do well and our clients would have all fired us if that&#39;s all we owned.&#34;</p><p>11. &#34;There&#39;s nothing wrong with being a bargain hunter. We check the price of everything we buy. Even if we go to Costco, my wife checks the price somewhere else.&#34;</p><p>12. &#34;A lot of the SPACs have been dressed up for the stock market, and there have been a lot of less-than-optimal results.&#34; - <em>Gabelli pointed to Nikola Motors as an example</em>.</p><p>13. &#34;Work from five to nine, your competitors are going to work from nine to five. Drink one less beer, one less coffee at an expensive coffee shop, and save the money each week. Then compound it at 2%, 4%, 6%, 8%, 10% over the next 40 years, and see what that gives you - economic flexibility.&#34; - <em>Gabelli&#39;s advice to young people.</em></p><p>14. &#34;You don&#39;t want to have wealth to have wealth. You want to have options, so that you can tell somebody what to do, as opposed to having someone tell you what to do. In addition to that, be passionate about what you do, because if you just want a job, you&#39;re not going to be happy.&#34;</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
