overreach","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/florida-school-law-sb-233-government-hypocritical-republicans-de-santis-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60edfe1fa8d8c00019b02ff2?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Ron DeSantis\" height=\"1000\" width=\"2000\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Florida Gov. Ron DeSantis speaks at a press conference at LifeScience Logistics.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Photo by Paul Hennessy/SOPA Images/LightRocket via Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Florida Republicans passed a law that mandates students and faculty to clarify their political beliefs.</li>\n<li>As an educator and former Republican, the new law is a terrible overreach of government.</li>\n<li>Colleges and universities should be realms of free expression, unmonitored by politicians.</li>\n<li>Matt Walton was the 2015 Republican nominee for the Virginia House of Delegates (74th District).</li>\n<li> </li>\n<li>This is an opinion column. The thoughts expressed are those of the author.</li>\n<li> </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>&#34;Tell us your political beliefs or else.&#34;</p><p>This is what will be required of Florida&#39;s public university students and faculty under a new law. Recently, the Republican Florida Legislature passed <a href=\"https://www.myfloridahouse.gov/Sections/Documents/loaddoc.aspx?FileName=_h0233er.docx&DocumentType=Bill&BillNumber=0233&Session=2021Session=2021\">SB 233</a>, which mandates the State Board of Education to conduct an annual survey of the &#34;intellectual freedom and viewpoint diversity&#34; on each campus. Once it was passed by the Legislature, it was signed into law by Republican Governor Ron DeSantis.</p><p>This bill will survey the staff and students at public universities about their political beliefs. The bill and the resulting surveys are dangerous and an overreach of the government. We should not compel universities to ask their employees or students about their political beliefs. This is big government and an intrusion into the rights of people.</p><h2>Survey says</h2><p>This bill stands in stark contrast to the <a href=\"https://www.gop.com/platform/renewing-american-values/\">Republican Platform</a>, in which they &#34;call on state officials to preserve our public colleges, universities, and trade schools as places of learning and the exchange of ideas, not zones of intellectual intolerance or &#39;safe zones,&#39; as if college students need protection from the free exchange of ideas.&#34;</p><p>SB 233 will intrude in the lives of students and staff on college campuses by asking them to fill out a survey about their beliefs. Proponents say that this is needed to make sure that there is an adequate representation of political views on campus. By their admission then, they are attempting to &#34;protect&#34; college students from varying views, a stark contradiction of the GOP platform.  </p><p>This bill was a solution for a problem that does not exist. In 2018 in Florida, the <a href=\"https://www.flsenate.gov/laws/statutes/2018/1004.097\">Campus Free Expression Act</a> went into effect to protect free expression in the public areas of the campuses. </p><p>One aspect of the bill could be to &#34;level&#34; the ideological makeup of campus faculty.t At face value, that sounds great. However, it&#39;s more dangerous than you think. Imagine a QAnon believer examining the survey results and stating that there is not enough representation on the faculty that supports these views and demanding that the university hire a QAnon faculty member, or even people calling for the addition of a Holocaust denier to the staff to satisfy someone&#39;s interpretation of a survey. This law has the potential to weaponize campus and turn them into cesspools of conspiracy theorists. </p><p>The security of the survey responses is another factor that has to be considered. With computer hacking happening at <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/06/05/business/leon-panetta-cyber-attacks.html\">unprecedented levels</a>, there is no guarantee that these survey results will remain anonymous. Foreign actors such as Russian, China, and Iran have made it a goal to sow hateful discourse in America and promote political chaos, especially in the 2016 presidential election. </p><p>Allan Liska, an intelligence analyst at Recorded Future <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/06/03/us/politics/ransomware-cybersecurity-infrastructure.html\">said</a> when discussing government cyber security, that &#34;&#34;Ransomware attacks are only going to get worse and more pervasive into people&#39;s lives, and they&#39;re not disappearing anytime soon.&#34;  It would be easy for a hostile country to hack these surveys and leak the results and responses in a way that would promote discord and division.   </p><p>Additionally, the law allows further intrusion into the educational environment in which it  guarantees the right to record classroom lectures and discussions. As a teacher, I can tell you that this is a recipe for disaster. </p><p>Recording someone without permission (or a warrant) a <a href=\"http://www.leg.state.fl.us/Statutes/index.cfm?App_mode=Display_Statute&Search_String=&URL=0900-0999/0934/Sections/0934.03.html.03.html\">felony</a> under Florida law, as Florida is a &#34;Two Party&#34; state where it is a crime to intercept or record a &#34;wire, oral, or electronic communication&#34;, unless all parties to the communication consent, something that many of my fellow educators would not allow. </p><p>Giving students universal control and the right to record teachers without their knowledge is a travesty. Imagine if a student who was angry over a recent grade recorded a teacher and baited them to say something out of context  and then posted the video on social media and ruined the teacher&#39;s reputation. In an era where Republican are fighting against &#34;cancel culture&#34; , recording teachers for their academic views for the intent of having them replaced would degrade an educational system that is the best in the world.</p><p>Republicans, especially Tea Party Republicans, for years have fought against government intrusion into people&#39;s lives, as many fought and <a href=\"https://www.aclu.org/other/conservative-voices-against-usa-patriot-act\">spoke out</a> against the Patriot Act. SB 233 not only allows universal surveillance into classrooms, but also pries into the political beliefs of students and faculty. </p><p>Colleges and universities should and must be a free expression of ideas and intellectual discovery. There is no need for the state to pry into the beliefs of students and staff by surveying their thoughts, something that you would see in more authoritative countries. We must promote educational environments that are meant to challenge students&#39; thoughts and not make professors feel as if big brother is watching at all times.</p><div Weisselberg and lawyers for the former president&#39;s company pleaded not guilty to the charges.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-organization-allen-weisselberg-terminated-scotland-golf-course-2021-7\">Insider first reported</a> last week on filings in the UK showing that Weisselberg quit his role with one of the Trump Organization&#39;s Scottish golf courses.</p><p>Documents filed Friday with the Florida Division of Corporations show <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-organization-allen-weisselberg-subsidiaries-leadership-tax-fraud-scandal-2021-7\">he resigned from other subsidiaries</a> as well. The Post <a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/trump-org-cfo-began-resigning-his-positions-days-before-he-was-indicted-documents-show/2021/07/13/aa698b8e-e41e-11eb-a41e-c8442c213fa8_story.html\">identified</a> 54 different subsidiaries from which Weisselberg resigned overall.</p><p>Prior to the indictments, prosecutors tried without success to &#34;flip&#34; Weisselberg into cooperating with their larger, ongoing investigation into the Trump Organization&#39;s finances.</p><p>In addition to the tax charges filed against Weisselberg and the company, Manhattan prosecutors <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-tax-returns-explainer-donald-trump-organization-2021-2\">had been reviewing</a> whether the Trump Organization broke financial laws by misrepresenting property values for favorable tax, loan, and insurance rates, or by facilitating a hush-money payment to adult film star Stormy Daniels over her claims that she had an affair with ex-President Donald Trump.</p><p>Lawyers for Weisselberg declined to comment. career.</p><p>McConnell&#39;s response came as the former president attacked retiring GOP Sen. Richard Shelby of Alabama for backing Katie Boyd Britt in the 2022 Senate race to succeed him in the upper chamber. Britt, a former chief of staff for Shelby, is <a href=\"https://www.bcatoday.org/katie-boyd-britt/\">currently</a> the president and CEO of the Business Council of Alabama.</p><p>Trump has thrown his support behind longtime ally and conservative Rep. Mo Brooks, who <a href=\"https://www.al.com/news/2021/07/mo-brooks-2020-election-stolen-from-donald-trump-kiss-ass-speech-distorted.html\">continues to support</a> the former president&#39;s claims of a &#34;stolen&#34; 2020 presidential election.</p><p>&#34;I see that the RINO Senator from Alabama, close friend of Old Crow Mitch McConnell, Richard Shelby, is pushing hard to have his &#39;assistant&#39; fight the great Mo Brooks for his Senate seat,&#34; Trump said in a statement. &#34;She is not in any way qualified and is certainly not what our Country needs or not what Alabama wants. For Mitch McConnell to be wasting money on her campaign is absolutely outrageous.&#34;</p><p><strong><em>Read more: </em></strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-white-house-administration-maga-alumni-network-database-2021-7?inline-read-more&inline-read-more&inline-read-more&inline-read-morene-read-more\"><em>Where is Trump&#39;s White House staff now? We created a searchable database of more than 327 top staffers to show where they all landed</em></a></p><p>Shelby, for his part, dismissed being called a &#34;RINO,&#34; or Republican in name only, a pejorative used by Trump for members of the party who he doesn&#39;t consider to be true conservatives.</p><p>&#34;I was a Democrat at one time,&#34; Shelby told CNN. &#34;A long time ago, we all were. I don&#39;t know if the president was. But I&#39;m a Republican. I don&#39;t think anybody questions that up here.&#34;</p><p>Shelby, who was first elected to the Senate as a Democrat in 1986 before switching to the GOP in 1994, expressed his continued support for Britt.</p><p>&#34;She&#39;s the best qualified and the best hope we&#39;ve got in the state,&#34; he said.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.wtvy.com/2021/07/11/brooks-britt-respond-trumps-statement-alabamas-senate-race/\">In a statement to Dothan-based WTVY News 4</a>, Britt said that the comments reflected fear from Brooks.</p><p>&#34;I don&#39;t need anyone else to fight my battles, and as Alabama&#39;s next US Senator, I won&#39;t be a rubber stamp for anyone,&#34; she said in a statement. &#34;My opponent is obviously panicked; he&#39;s been in elected office for 40 years, but the people of Alabama are eager for a real conservative choice and someone who&#39;s going to bring change to DC.&#34;</p><p>McConnell&#39;s super PAC, the Senate Leadership Fund, has not yet endorsed a candidate in the race. The senator did not respond to CNN&#39;s question about whether the group will direct money to the contest in the heavily Republican state.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/mcconnell-responds-trump-old-crow-insult-alabama-republican-senate-race-2021-7'>Business Insider</a></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:F7zBnMyn0Lo\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:V_sGLiPBpWU\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:V_sGLiPBpWU\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:qj6IDK7rITs\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?a=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:gIN9vFwOqvQ\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:gIN9vFwOqvQ\" border=\"0\"></img></a>\n</div><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/J-GrTmgEkbs\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 14 Jul 2021 15:37:20 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/607582c32cc1ef0018da1626?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"50cf6b12b1d3852a0bcc1253ca37aa82","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn78@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-34-00-902_3429f457a1c08dac.webp","destWidth":1728,"destHeight":1296,"sourceBytes":106152,"destBytes":106152,"author":"insider@insider.com (John L. Dorman)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/5fecf9a49ff41f001883f7a1?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn18@2020_1/2021/07/14/17-34-04-074_95a557760a2843cd.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn5@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-04-185_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn86@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-04-335_62e3136aa5735ed6.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn78@2020_4/2021/07/14/17-34-02-656_a3c9a57b5a2e49c5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn85@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-02-502_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=J-GrTmgEkbs:8YONIVpEnS8:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn33@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-04-202_9ee3bbbc13df2bc1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/J-GrTmgEkbs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn41@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-34-02-751_858a77388d7ba6fb.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626284019893},{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"I've been on more than 15 cruises and just got back from Royal Caribbean's 7-day voyage. Here's how to have the best possible experience while traveling at sea.","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-to-know-advice-plan-cruise-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ddc8c3cad1220011caf72f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Halee Whiting\" height=\"2652\" width=\"3536\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Halee Whiting.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Halee Whiting</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Halee Whiting, 32, is a frequent traveler and cruise enthusiast - she even got married on one.</li>\n<li>She recommends working with a travel agent, getting insurance, and bringing a portable laundry bin.</li>\n<li>Here&#39;s her advice for new cruise-goers, as told to freelancer Jamie Killin.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>I&#39;m a <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/no-hesitations-book-cruise-royal-carribbean-best-way-vacation-2021-6\">frequent cruise-goer</a> and travel blogger with my own hotel sales consultation company.</p><p>I&#39;ve cruised more than 15 times - including on one of the first cruises to embark since the pandemic. This is what I wish I knew before booking my first cruise.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/royal-caribbean-vaccinated-cruise-safe-pandemic-hurt-tourism-2021-7\">I went on Royal Caribbean&#39;s 7-day cruise to the Bahamas. I felt completely safe, but my heart broke seeing how hurt the tourism industry is.</a></em></p><h2><strong>One of the biggest things I would recommend for people who haven&#39;t cruised before is finding a travel agent or advisor who specializes in cruises.</strong></h2><p>Even with me being in the industry for as long as I have, having a travel agent is helpful.</p><p>When I got married, I did a wedding cruise, and we had our ceremony in Nassau on the beach. We had a two-hour cocktail reception, then got back on the cruise.</p><p>I decided to use a travel agent because I didn&#39;t want all the guests calling me, but this travel agent was with a bigger agency and the experience was awful. I almost felt like I was telling her how to do her job.</p><p>She wasn&#39;t very flexible and I swore off using an agent. Then, I ended up joining a cruise community on Facebook, which is a huge thing because cruising is so social, and I had to book through their travel agent to go on our group cruise.</p><p>The agent and I ended up talking - and we&#39;re now best friends four years later. We even host a weekly travel talk show together going over travel news for our little travel community that we created on Facebook this year. Working with him was just a totally different experience.</p><p>When I was doing a trip this past August, my plane ended up being rerouted because of a windstorm, so we ended up landing at an airport and had to clear customs there and wait for the plane to fuel up.</p><p>It was 8 p.m. on Saturday, and I called him and he told me what I could purchase and have covered through my travel insurance. He had me send him all my receipts, submitted it all to the travel insurance company, and got me refunds for my hotel, meals, and flight.</p><p>Travel agents don&#39;t cost money - they make their commissions from the ships and travel insurance agencies or tour companies. They also get access to a completely different set of rates than Expedia or what you see online.</p><p>If somebody&#39;s preparing to go on a cruise during the pandemic, using a travel agent is huge even if you&#39;re a seasoned cruiser because the guidelines keep changing, and it&#39;s their job to stay on top of it.</p><h2><strong>Travel insurance is also great because it covers anything from medical issues to trip interruption or even theft.</strong></h2><p>I&#39;d never had travel insurance until my travel agent educated me on it, but it&#39;s been helpful already. I had my phone stolen in Paris last year and my travel insurance covered it.</p><p>Some people I know kind of don&#39;t want to spend the money, but for my husband, my daughter, and I for our two cruises at the end of August it cost $225 total. So worth it.</p><p>It&#39;s not necessarily the medical aspect that gets used the majority of the time - it&#39;s trip interruption, the hiccups, and things of that nature.</p><h2><strong>I also recommend doing your research.</strong></h2><p>Watch a cruise-ship tour video and stateroom tour videos. There are websites like <a href=\"https://www.cruisecritic.com/\">Cruise Critic</a>, where people rate certain room types. You could, for example, see if anybody has stayed in Adventure of the Sea room 9244 and see the reviews on that.</p><p>My husband&#39;s a bigger guy, and the stateroom showers are kind of like tubes, so if you&#39;re a big and tall guy you might need to research what room you&#39;re booking to know what&#39;s best for you and what will be comfortable.</p><p>What people don&#39;t realize is, online they&#39;re going to have pictures of their newest and greatest ships, and not all the pictures online are completely accurate to what your room is going to look like. If you&#39;re seeing videos and pictures of Symphony of the Seas and you go and book the Brilliance of the Seas, you&#39;re frankly going to be a little disappointed.</p><p>I&#39;ve had cruise regret on certain ship types that I&#39;ve booked because it was cheap. And there are certain classes of ships that are not for me.</p><h2><strong>Join Facebook groups to meet people ahead of your cruise.</strong></h2><p>I&#39;ve met so many new people because of cruises. Facebook, as much as it&#39;s an older social-media platform, is a great hub for the cruise experience.</p><p>There are a lot of groups to choose from, too - for example, there will be a group called Adventure of the Sea June 12 that you can join and ask questions and meet with people going on the same cruise ahead of time.</p><p>You can also go to Instagram and search hashtags for your different cruises and you&#39;ll see content creators and bloggers that cruise and even other cruise-goers you can connect with. You&#39;ll also find people such as myself doing lives every week and answering questions.</p><h2><strong>There are things you can bring to make your room - which is typically much smaller than a hotel room - more comfortable.</strong></h2><p>For example, I bring magnetic hooks because your walls are metal to hang my bathrobe or different things from them. I also bring a pop-up hamper for laundry. Little cruise-packing hacks.</p><p>Another thing people don&#39;t realize is you have very limited outlets, so I have a multiport charging outlet.</p><h2><strong>Before my first post-pandemic cruise, I wish we had a little more information about what the onboard experience was going to be like.</strong></h2><p>I don&#39;t think I was emotionally prepared enough for how different the environment would be with the mass reduction of people onboard and how the COVID-19 protocols altered the social experience.</p><p>Another thing people need to be aware of is it&#39;s not just knowing what your cruise line protocols are - you need to keep up with your port-of-call protocols. My friend is on a cruise right now, and Barbados required masks the whole way through.</p><p>You need to be flexible, and you need to make a conscious decision about purchasing from a line that aligns with your values and wants.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/what-to-know-advice-plan-cruise-2021-7'>Business Insider</a></div><div src=\"https://i.insider.com/5ef628405af6cc78717045d7?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Trump Hannity\" height=\"1250\" width=\"2500\" charset=\"\"> \n  <figcaption>\n   President Donald Trump and Fox News host Sean Hannity. \n   <p class=\"copyright\">Ethan Miller/Getty Images</p> \n  </figcaption> </img>\n</figure>\n<ul class=\"summary-list\"> \n <li>Facebook's best-performing pages in the US often are entirely right and far-right wing publications. </li> \n <li>The data demonstrating as much comes from Facebook's own measurement tool, CrowdTangle.</li> \n <li>In private, Facebook execs have reportedly bristled at the data tool and what it shows. </li> \n <li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">Visit the Business section of Insider for more stories</a>.</li> \n</ul>\n<p>Despite claims by some Republican politicians led by former President Trump that social media sites censor conservative views, Facebook's data makes it clear: The social network's best performing content is almost entirely from right and far-right wing publications and personalities.</p>\n<p>That's according to CrowdTangle, a Facebook-owned and operated service that has reportedly caused Facebook executives to bristle at what the tool shows to the public.</p>\n<p>\"Our own tools are helping journos to consolidate the wrong narrative,\" Facebook VP of global affairs Nick Clegg said in an internal company email, <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/07/14/technology/inside-facebooks-data-wars.html\">according to a new report by The New York Times</a>. Like Facebook's advertising transparency tools, Crowdtangle has been repeatedly used to demonstrate major criticisms of the tech and social media giant - criticisms that Facebook execs would rather not have to defend in public.</p>\n<p>Perhaps most prominent is a Twitter tool created by New York Times tech writer Kevin Roose automatically pulls data from Crowdtangle every day that shows, \"the top-performing link posts by US Facebook pages in the last 24 hours, ranked by total interactions.\"</p>\n<p>To break that down: Posts containing links to something outside of Facebook that were shared within the last 24 hours by a US-based Facebook page. And the list is ranked from 1 to 10 depending on total \"interactions\" - which includes \"reactions, shares, and comments,\" according to Roose.</p>\n<p>As the data shows, <a href=\"https://twitter.com/FacebooksTop10\">the most-engaged pages top 10 list</a> is consistently dominated by the likes of Fox News host Sean Hannity, conservative commentator Ben Shapiro, and Christian evangelist Franklin Graham.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet blockquote\" data-lang=\"en\" data-cards=\"\" data-conversation=\"\">\n -Facebook's Top 10 (@FacebooksTop10) \n <a href=\"https://twitter.com/mims/statuses/1414993359551156224?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">July 13, 2021</a>\n</blockquote>\n<script async=\"\" src=\"//platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script>\n<p>Before he was banned from Facebook following the January 6 attempted insurrection, Trump's pages dominated the lists.</p>\n<p>That, among other metrics, is what led to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/trump-mark-zuckerberg-dinner-number-one-facebook-2020-1\">Facebook CEO Mark Zuckerberg telling Trump he was \"number one\"</a> on the social media platform in late 2019.</p>\n<p>Internally, Facebook execs are reportedly divided over what to do with Crowdtangle and its data. Some Facebook execs are said to have argued for more data transparency, but others are said to have argued against the potential for more negative stories about Facebook to emerge. </p>\n<p>\"Facebook would love full transparency if there was a guarantee of positive stories and outcomes,\" former Facebook VP Brian Boland told the Times. \"But when transparency creates uncomfortable moments, their reaction is often to shut down the transparency.\"</p>\n<p>Part of the reason Boland left Facebook, he says, is because, \"the company does not want to invest in understanding the impact of its core products.\" </p>\n<p>Facebook representatives didn't respond to a request for comment as of publishing, but Facebook spokesperson Joe Osborne told the Times that Crowdtangle, \"is part of a growing suite of transparency resources we've made available for people, including academics and journalists\" and that the company is, \"developing a more comprehensive strategy for how we build on some of these transparency efforts moving forward.\"</p>\n<p><em><strong>Got a tip?</strong> Contact Insider senior correspondent Ben Gilbert via email (<a href=\"mailto:bgilbert@insider.com\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">bgilbert@insider.com</a>),</em><em> or Twitter DM (<a href=\"https://twitter.com/RealBenGilbert\" data-analytics-module=\"body_link\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"100\">@realbengilbert</a>). 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"Twitch emotes: Everything to know about Twitch's wildly popular take on emoji","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/twitch-emotes","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ee1be6a8d8c00019b03051?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A selection of Twitch emotes: Kappa, LUL, Jebaited, and PogChamp.\" height=\"398\" width=\"796\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Twitch emotes have a wide variety of meanings and uses.\n<p class=\"copyright\">William Antonelli/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Twitch emotes are small emoji-like icons that you can use in any Twitch streamer&#39;s chat room.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">Twitch streamers with enough viewers can upload their own custom emotes for subscribers to use.</li>\n<li aria-level=\"1\">If you download the third-party extension BetterTTV, you can access dozens of new Twitch emotes for free.</li>\n<li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/tech-reference\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\" data-analytics-module=\"summary_bullets\" data-analytics-post-depth=\"0\"><strong>Visit Insider&#39;s Tech Reference library for more stories</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>To the untrained eye, reading a Twitch chat can feel like interpreting hieroglyphic code. That&#39;s because Twitch chats are packed with the streaming social media site&#39;s popular &#34;emotes.&#34;</p><p>Fortunately, we&#39;re here to help get you up to speed on Twitch emotes: Which ones are the most popular and what they mean, where to click and what to type to send emotes in Twitch chat, and how you can create your own signature emotes.</p><h2>Twitch emotes, explained</h2><p>Twitch emotes are tiny pictures that, just like emoji, each have their own meaning and connotation. And although some have an obvious use, most of them are pretty obscure. You can send an emote on Twitch to quickly convey to a streamer and fellow chatters your emotional reaction or opinion; whatever your mood, there&#39;s probably a suitable emote.</p><p>A few dozen emotes are available to everyone on the site; these are called &#34;global&#34; emotes. Once a channel gains a certain amount of subscribers, they gain the ability to add their own exclusive emotes that only subscribers can use.</p><p>Some emotes are only available to users who have Amazon Prime or <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-cheer-on-twitch\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">donate &#34;bits,&#34;</a> and others require you to install an extension called BetterTTV (which we&#39;ll discuss below).</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ee14d761b8600019f16ee8?format=jpeg\" alt=\"xQc&#39;s Twitch channel, with dozens of emotes in the chat box.\" height=\"1800\" width=\"2880\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Chatters flood popular Twitch streamer “xQc” with various emotes in chat.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><h3>Using emotes</h3><p>To send an emote, simply type the name of the emote. For instance, to send the Kappa emote, you&#39;d type out &#34;Kappa&#34; and hit send.</p><p>You can also type a colon, start writing the name of your emote, and then select the emote from a drop-down list that will appear as you type.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ee170961b8600019f16eec?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A Twitch channel and chat, with the emote Kappa appearing in the search menu.\" height=\"638\" width=\"1276\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>You can type an emote&#39;s name out, or search for it.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Failing that, you can click the smiley face icon in the chat box to get a list of every available emote. Just click one to add it to your chat message.</p><aside class=\"breakout-box headline-regular\"><h2><strong>A selection of the most popular Twitch emotes</strong></h2><ul><li aria-level=\"1\"><strong>Kappa:</strong> A classic emote, Kappa is a smirking face in grayscale that signals sarcasm.</li><li aria-level=\"1\"><strong>LUL:</strong> The laughing face is Twitch&#39;s take on &#34;LOL.&#34;</li><li aria-level=\"1\"><strong>Jebaited:</strong> This bemused face is sent to signal that the streamer&#39;s been tricked or &#34;baited.&#34;</li><li aria-level=\"1\"><strong>PogChamp:</strong> Possibly the most popular emote on the site (<a href=\"https://www.polygon.com/2021/2/12/22280777/twitch-pogchamp-vote-results-lizard-meme-komodohype\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">and one of the most controversial</a>), you&#39;ll send this happy lizard when something awesome or exciting happens.</li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ee15b4a8d8c00019b03040?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A selection of Twitch emotes: Kappa, LUL, Jebaited, and PogChamp.\" height=\"614\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A selection of Twitch emotes: Kappa, LUL, Jebaited, and PogChamp.\n<p class=\"copyright\">William Antonelli/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure></aside><p>However, some of the most popular emotes require you use to use a browser extension called Better TwitchTV, or just BetterTTV for short.</p><h2>How to get more Twitch emotes with BetterTTV</h2><p>To use BetterTTV and get access to more Twitch emotes, you need to download the BetterTTV extension for your web browser, <a href=\"https://chrome.google.com/webstore/detail/betterttv/ajopnjidmegmdimjlfnijceegpefgped?hl=en\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Chrome</a>, <a href=\"https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/betterttv/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Firefox</a>, or <a href=\"https://microsoftedge.microsoft.com/addons/detail/betterttv/icllegkipkooaicfmdfaloehobmglglb\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Edge</a>.</p><p>Once you&#39;ve downloaded it:</p><p><strong>1.</strong> Head to any Twitch chat and select the &#34;Chat Settings&#34; gear icon in the bottom-right corner, by the stream chat window.</p><p><strong>2.</strong> Select &#34;BetterTTV Settings&#34; from the Chat Settings menu.</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ee1841a8d8c00019b03049?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The Twitch chat settings menu, with BetterTTV settings highlighted.\" height=\"638\" width=\"1276\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Open the BetterTTV settings menu.\n<p class=\"copyright\">William Antonelli/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p><strong>3.</strong> In the BetterTTV settings, make sure the &#34;BetterTTV Emote Menu,&#34; &#34;BetterTTV Emotes,&#34; and &#34;BetterTTV GIF Emotes,&#34; and &#34;FrankerFaceZ Emotes&#34; are all set to &#34;On.&#34;</p><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ee191ca8d8c00019b0304a?format=jpeg\" alt=\"The BetterTTV menu.\" height=\"1440\" width=\"2880\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Turn on all the extra BetterTTV emotes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Emma Witman/Insider</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>You&#39;ll now be able to use new BetterTTV and FrankerFaceZ &#34;Global&#34; emotes on every channel. Every Twitch streamer can also add up to 15 &#34;Channel&#34; emotes that anyone with BetterTTV can use in their chat.</p><h2>How to make your own Twitch emotes</h2><p>Along with global and BetterTTV emotes, every Twitch channel can submit their own custom emotes for subscribers to use. They&#39;re one of the unique ways that viewers can show their love for the channel.</p><p>However, to upload custom emotes, your Twitch channel needs to reach &#34;partner&#34; or &#34;affiliate&#34; status. Once there, you can take advantage of the tools provided in the Twitch Creator Dashboard to upload unique emotes.</p><ul><li>Twitch affiliates can have one emote for all subscribers, and two emotes each for $9.99 and $24.99 tier subscribers.</li><li>Twitch partners start with six emote slots, but that number can increase up to 60 as they earn more subscribers. Once you&#39;ve unlocked an emote slot, you get to keep it forever, even if you lose subscribers.</li></ul><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ee1a10a8d8c00019b0304e?format=jpeg\" alt=\"A selection of example custom emotes.\" height=\"1001\" width=\"849\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>A selection of example custom emotes.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Twitch</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Your emotes will have to meet a few parameters. To use <a href=\"https://help.twitch.tv/s/article/subscriber-emote-guide?language=en_US\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Twitch&#39;s auto-resize feature,</a> your file will need to be a square image between 112x112 and 4096x4096 pixels, and be a maximum of 1MB in size. Alternatively, you can use the manual mode by uploading the file in three sizes (28x28, 56x56, 112x112 pixels) that are 100kb in size or less. </p><p>Emotes also have to follow content rules; that means no depictions of hate, violence, sex, or targeted harassment are allowed.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"related-article-module-end-of-article\" class=\"mceNonEditable\"><a data-type=\"5ebc618ce3c3fb30a1485fb3\" data-title=\"How to subscribe to a channel on Twitch to show your support and unlock exclusive features\" data-url=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-to-subscribe-on-twitch\" data-vertical=\"sai\" data-image=\"https://i.insider.com/5ebc5f88fc593d30950d0ef5\">How to subscribe to a channel on Twitch to show your support and unlock exclusive features</a><a data-type=\"60ba487516fb072c977c4549\" data-title=\"What does 'TOS' mean? 7@2020_5/2021/07/14/17-34-00-785_1245c64ec0cb93e1.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/PDJ6PsukGS0":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn74@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-34-04-366_5969402a83bc3d73.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626284019905},{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"The CEO of a freight-booking company explains the reason behind shipping delays: 'It's simple, Americans are buying more stuff'","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/freight-shipping-delays-caused-by-americans-buying-more-stuff-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/5b6a08875124c9285c944760?format=jpeg\" alt=\"FILE PHOTO - Shipping containers are seen at the port in Shanghai, China April 10, 2018. REUTERS/Aly Song/File Photo\" height=\"533\" width=\"800\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>FILE PHOTO - Shipping containers are seen at the port in Shanghai\n<p class=\"copyright\">Thomson Reuters</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>In an interview with <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/videos/2021-07-13/could-take-a-few-years-for-ships-to-catch-up-to-demand-freightos-ceo-video?sref=BWbpWjRm\">Bloomberg</a>, the CEO of Freightos walked through what is causing shipping delays.</li>\n<li>Your favorite brands are paying <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/shipping-crisis-causing-shortages-why-2021-6\">10 times the typical price</a> of shipping your stuff across the ocean.</li>\n<li>It could take years to build enough ships to catch up with demand, Bloomberg reported. </li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>The founder and CEO of online freight-booking platform Freightos walked through the main challenges fueling the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/shipping-crisis-causing-shortages-why-2021-6\">global shipping crisis</a> in an <a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/videos/2021-07-13/could-take-a-few-years-for-ships-to-catch-up-to-demand-freightos-ceo-video?sref=BWbpWjRm\">interview with Bloomberg</a> on Tuesday. </p><p>&#34;It&#39;s simple,&#34; Zvi Schreiber said. &#34;Americans are buying more stuff.&#34; </p><p>The demand for imported goods is so high that shipping companies are racing to build more boats, a construction process that could take several years. </p><p>&#34;These are big big ships,&#34; Schreiber told Bloomberg. &#34;So when Americans suddenly change their buying habits ... it&#39;s going to take the industry a while to catch up.&#34; </p><p>The 2-day-shipping many customers have become accustomed to depends on a global supply chain that allows brands to transport products across the ocean and onto your doorstep.</p><p>Now, brands are paying 10 times the price of typical shipping costs - and some companies can&#39;t even get products onto a boat in the first place. </p><p>Brands are taking drastic measures to sidestep the crisis. <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/home-depot-container-ship-over-delays-rising-shipping-costs-2021-6\">Home Depot contracted its own ship</a> in hopes of avoiding delays and rising prices. After a year of customers complaining about month-long delays, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/peloton-spends-100m-expedited-shipping-2021-2\">Peloton spent $100 million</a> to expedite deliveries.</p><p>&#34;The pandemic broke the supply chain last year, and the shipping companies that move stuff all over the world still haven&#39;t recovered,&#34; <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/shipping-crisis-causing-shortages-why-2021-6\">Insider&#39;s Rachel Premack reported in June.</a></p><p>Schreiber told Bloomberg that while large corporations like Walmart can leverage company connections to place its orders on mega-ships in time, smaller and mid-sized brands get &#34;squeezed out.&#34; </p><p>In order for the world&#39;s shipping system to function, three elements are required: massive ships, containers on the ships, and places for the ships to park so that the containers can be unloaded. </p><p>While the price of shipping containers has <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/shipping-stocks-evergreen-price-transport-rates-container-crisis-supply-chain-2021-6\">skyrocketed</a>, Schreiber said that the industry simply does not have enough massive ships to keep up with America&#39;s outsized demand. </p><p>The only scenario in which Schreiber can foresee shipping timelines returning to pre-pandemic levels is if <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/how-the-global-shipping-crisis-ends-shortages-2021-6\">people start ordering fewer things.</a></p><p>&#34;It&#39;s hard to predict the future,&#34; Schreiber said. &#34;As restaurants and travel reopen, people may just spend a little less on stuff and that will solve the problem very quickly.&#34; </p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the 2021 14:09:49 +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/60eef01261b8600019f16ffd?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"3cccc5461c65a0ab0492f5395d839866","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn8@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-33-40-074_2e48113ace151f6c.webp","destWidth":1571,"destHeight":1178,"sourceBytes":127504,"destBytes":127504,"author":"kmclaughlin@businessinsider.com (Kelly McLaughlin)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/60eef01261b8600019f16ffd?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn8@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-33-40-074_2e48113ace151f6c.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn5@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-04-185_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=JShAtb1hf5o:3G5-uyI3DgA:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn41@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-34-04-547_ca3d8f409f9285b0.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=JShAtb1hf5o:3G5-uyI3DgA:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn74@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-03-376_900660787a6afac4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn85@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-02-502_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=JShAtb1hf5o:3G5-uyI3DgA:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn97@2020_6/2021/07/14/17-34-03-916_651f9076bf9cd113.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/JShAtb1hf5o":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn10@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-34-04-720_450cc733f2192cb1.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626284019906},{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"What is inflation and when you should really start worrying about it","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/what-is-inflation-runaway-hyperinflation-price-growth-interest-rates-fed-2021-5","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/609ac7abba78eb001906eb24?format=jpeg\" alt=\"GettyImages 1002925420\" height=\"2246\" width=\"4493\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Some investors worry that fiscal and monetary stimulus will drive up inflation.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Eva Hambach/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Infaltion rose 0.9% from May to June, higher than the consensus estimate of 0.5%.</li>\n<li>Where most expect inflation to be temporary, others fear a dangerous spiral, or &#34;runaway&#34; inflation.</li>\n<li>Here&#39;s what you need to know about inflation, where it stands today, and when you should start to worry.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>After decades of weaker-than-expected price growth, America has inflation on the brain.</p><p>Inflation - or the general rate at which prices climb - has taken center stage as the US economy climbs out of its year-long slump. Economists expected the combination of a swift reopening and trillions of dollars in stimulus would lift prices at their fastest rate in recent history, and it soared to its fastest rate since 2008 in the spring. After a brief dip, June&#39;s number came in higher than expected, fueled by big price increases for <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/price-of-used-cars-record-increase-june-2021-7\">used cars</a> and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/beef-pork-prices-rising-inflation-when-food-costs-could-fall-2021-7\">some food like beef and pork</a>.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/inflation-stimulus-debate-economic-growth-spending-federal-reserve-larry-summers-2021-3\">For some</a>, forecasts of stronger inflation bring up memories of the 1970s and 1980s, an era sometimes called the Great Inflation, when prices grew at such a furious pace that the Federal Reserve had to lift interest rates to historic highs.</p><p><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/millennials-boomers-inflation-fears-age-gap-stimulus-economic-growth-recovery-2021-3\">For younger observers</a>, healthy inflation is a long pursued but seldom seen goal. Price growth has trended below the Fed&#39;s 2% target for most of the past quarter-century. People under 40 simply don&#39;t know a world with runaway inflation - or what the beginning of such a world might look like.</p><p>But recent economic headlines - gas shortages, troubles in the labor market, and big-government programs - have a distinctly &#39;70s flair. Just when should Americans know when to be really worried that inflation could be back in a big and problematic way?</p><p>Here&#39;s a look at what inflation actually is, why it&#39;s a tricky concept that is a bit of a self-fulfilling prophecy, and how it&#39;s actually unfolding in 2021.</p><bi-shortcode id=\"table-of-contents-sticky\" class=\"mceNonEditable\" data-type=\"h2\">Table of Contents: Masthead Sticky</bi-shortcode><h2>Why are people worried about inflation?</h2><p>The basic notion of soaring prices is concerning. Roughly 9.3 million Americans are still out of work, and millions more were unemployed for at least some of the past year. At a time when many Americans are looking for stable financial footing, people are more worried about inflation <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/inflation-expectations-outlook-rise-us-economy-reopening-spending-price-growth-2021-5\">than they have been in years</a>.</p><p>The way in which prices have been climbing has already made some worried. While the Fed and President Joe Biden&#39;s Council of Economic Advisors have repeatedly said they expect stronger inflation to be only temporary, others are less optimistic.</p><p>Former Treasury Secretary Larry Summers, one of the loudest voices raising concerns of rampant price growth, castigated Democrats&#39; $1.9 trillion stimulus in March as the &#34;least responsible&#34; fiscal policy in 40 years and kindling for an inflation crisis.</p><p>&#34;I think there&#39;s about a one-third chance that the Fed and the Treasury will get what they&#39;re hoping for and we&#39;ll get rapid growth that will moderate in a non-inflationary way,&#34; he added.</p><p>A return to the inflation seen in the 1970s would be disastrous for the already ailing economy. In that decade, swaths of easy money were initially viewed as a way to combat unemployment, but inflation quickly broke out of its trend and spiraled out of control. The Fed was forced to step in with interest rates as high as 20% to choke off the price growth, and that had its own detrimental effects on the economy, including a deep recession in the early 1980s.</p><p>Conservative economists have warned Biden&#39;s $1.9 trillion stimulus package was unnecessary and could spark a similar disaster. Whether price growth stays elevated or trends back to about 2% will tell the tale of whether Biden&#39;s plan was safe or fuel for a 1970s-like crash.</p><h2>What would healthy inflation look like this year?</h2><p>The Fed, America&#39;s central bank, has an &#34;inflation target,&#34; which it uses to guide price growth. In a major shift, the central bank replaced its 2% target in August with a goal for inflation that averages 2% over time. This update allows the Fed to pursue inflation above 2% immediately after the crisis as it tries to run the economy hot and drive a stronger recovery.</p><p>The Fed&#39;s own projections point to the stronger-but-transitory inflation it expects to see over the next few months. Policymakers expect year-over-year personal consumption expenditures - the Fed&#39;s preferred inflation measure - to reach 3% this year before cooling to 2.1% in 2022, according to a <a href=\"https://www.federalreserve.gov/monetarypolicy/files/fomcprojtabl20210616.pdf\">June release</a>.</p><p>The Fed&#39;s new inflation target opens the door for a period of economic overheating as the country reopens. It&#39;s this gamble that concerns conservative economists, or &#34;hawks.&#34; After decades of not letting inflation trend above 2%, it&#39;s embarking on an experiment to let the country run hot in hopes of a faster recovery.</p><p>Fed Chair Jerome Powell has been less exact with his forecast, but expects inflation to trend above 2% for &#34;some time&#34; before falling in line with the central bank&#39;s long-term goal.</p><h2>How does inflation look now?</h2><p>Signs of an inflation pick-up have emerged, which the Fed says it expected and critics say merits caution.</p><p>The PCE price index <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/pce-inflation-may-price-growth-economic-data-reopening-spending-surge-2021-6\">jumped 0.4% in May</a>, marking a slowdown from price growth seen in March and April. Economists expected a 0.5% jump last month. The measure also notched a 3.9% year-over-year gain, the fastest annual rate since August 2008.</p><p>Still, the comparison is somewhat skewed by last year&#39;s weak readings. Inflation &#34;doves&#34; say such a big jump is only natural after the pandemic and widespread lockdowns brought price growth to a near crawl.</p><p>The core PCE price index, which excludes volatile food and energy prices, rose 0.5% in April and 3.4% on a year-over-year basis. The core measure is the Fed&#39;s preferred gauge of nationwide price growth.</p><p>Separately, the Consumer Price Index <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/consumer-price-index-inflation-june-2021-7\" rel=\"nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">showed prices climbing 0.9% from May to June</a>. The gauge rose 5.4% year-over-year, also indicating the strongest inflation since 2008.</p><p>Inflation expectations are also a gauge worth watching. Median US inflation expectations for the next 12 months gained to 4% in May from 3.4%, according to the <a href=\"https://www.newyorkfed.org/newsevents/news/research/2021/20210614\">Federal Reserve Bank of New York</a>. Expectations can serve as a kind of self-fulfilling prophecy. When Americans anticipate faster price growth, businesses tend to lift prices and workers in turn demand higher wages. While inflation expectations typically surpass real inflation, they can hint at the direction inflation will trend, and even affect prices and wages in that direction.</p><h2>What can the Fed and the government do about inflation?</h2><p>Inflation has been half of the Fed&#39;s dual mandate since its inception in 1913. The central bank was tasked by Congress to ensure stable price growth for the US economy. Its main lever for doing so is its benchmark interest rate, which dictates borrowing costs across the country.</p><p>When rates are high, Americans are more incentivized to save money. When rates are low, or near zero as they are today, Americans are pushed to borrow and spend. The Fed&#39;s ability to change rates allows it to stimulate economic activity in times of recession or cool spending when the economy is running hot.</p><p>The latter is primarily how the Fed dampens strong inflation. By raising interest rates, the central bank weakens the incentive to borrow and spend. That then drags on demand and weakens the rate at which businesses lift prices.</p><p>Powell said in March that lifting its threshold for future rate hikes can allow it to <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/fed-powell-march-fomc-asset-purchases-central-bank-monetary-policy-2021-3\">more aggressively pursue its maximum-employment target</a>.</p><section data-track-content=\"\" data-post-type=\"post\"><p>&#34;There was a time when there was a tight connection between unemployment and inflation. That time is long gone,&#34; he said. &#34;We had low unemployment in 2018 and 2019 and the beginning of &#39;20 without having troubling inflation at all.&#34;</p><p>During those years, unemployment and wage growth among low-income households and racial minorities started to fall in line with broader measures. By letting inflation run above its historical average for some time, the Fed aims to foster not just a tighter labor market, but one that&#39;s more inclusive and beneficial for all Americans.</p><p>The risk is that higher inflation in pursuit of a more inclusive economy can spark a new crisis as price growth runs out of control.</p></section><div class=\"read-original\">Read the +0000","feedId":22,"bgimg":"https://i.insider.com/608afa2134af8d0018599f8c?format=jpeg","linkMd5":"163295cd2bb6965be631841cf3f6150e","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn2@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-05-022_45f85eed86674553.webp","destWidth":4276,"destHeight":3207,"sourceBytes":339188,"destBytes":339188,"author":"bwinck@businessinsider.com (Ben Winck,Bartie Scott)","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://i.insider.com/609ac7abba78eb001906eb24?format=jpeg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn91@2020_1/2021/07/14/17-34-01-669_732bb4104ed36222.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx13/cdn5@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-04-185_cc3ef43fc8ff5801.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zhjeO_NwFbI:G1B-UTvON_Y:F7zBnMyn0Lo":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx6/cdn96@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-00-742_191733d14703d4c3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zhjeO_NwFbI:G1B-UTvON_Y:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn19@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-01-859_c10d09ea6e60aa63.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx14/cdn85@2020_2/2021/07/14/17-34-02-502_740defb435ea442b.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/businessinsider?i=zhjeO_NwFbI:G1B-UTvON_Y:gIN9vFwOqvQ":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn71@2020_1/2021/07/14/17-34-00-762_99750107a5100dcc.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/businessinsider/~4/zhjeO_NwFbI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx15/cdn5@2020_3/2021/07/14/17-34-04-704_22497f4288e8f522.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1626284019906},{"createdTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","updatedTime":"2021-07-15 01:33:39","title":"Parents are gearing up to spend big on back-to-school stuff, boosted by pandemic savings and the new child tax credit payments","link":"https://www.businessinsider.com/back-to-school-season-spending-starts-early-higher-2021-7","description":"<figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60ecadffca74780018ae8f97?format=jpeg\" alt=\"Mother and daughter wearing face masks and looking at school supplies in a store. The daughter is wearing a blue backpack.\" height=\"1357\" width=\"1809\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>\n<p class=\"copyright\">CasarsaGuru/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>While kids anticipate the return to school, parents are ready to buy supplies early and spend more.</li>\n<li>According to Deloitte, K-12 spending could be $32.5 billion this year, 16% higher than last year.</li>\n<li>Some Americans may spend child tax credit payments, which will go out on July 15, on school supplies.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/?hprecirc-bullet\">See more stories on Insider&#39;s business page</a>.</li>\n</ul><p>As the school year approaches, some children will <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/biden-schools-should-reopen-fall-in-person-learning-2021-4\">say goodbye to virtual learning</a> and hello to a lot of new back-to-school clothes, shoes, and other items needed for in-person learning.</p><p>A recent <a href=\"https://www2.deloitte.com/content/dam/insights/articles/7192_cii_back-to-school-interactive/DI_Back-to-school-survey.pdf\">Deloitte</a> report found parents are gearing up to spend more on back-to-school shopping than in 2019, and that they are ready to start buying school supplies earlier than the back-to-school season typically begins. The report points to a possible reason why: half of respondents said they&#39;re worried items will be out of stock.</p><p>Plus, experts say parents&#39; spending will be boosted by higher-than-normal savings and the new child tax credit starting this week from the federal government.</p><h2>The new child tax credits could help parents foot the bill </h2><p>Many parents will start receiving monthly <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/irs-child-tax-credit-payment-dates-families-monthly-payments-2021-6\">child tax credit payments </a>of $250 or $300 per child this week through December. The payments may help with retail sales for items like food and school supplies as reported by <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/07/12/child-tax-credit-payments-may-boost-retail-sales-as-soon-as-this-month.html\">CNBC</a>.</p><p>&#34;It&#39;s a good thing for Walmart and grocery stores,&#34; Jim Sullivan, an economics professor at the University of Notre Dame, told <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/07/12/child-tax-credit-payments-may-boost-retail-sales-as-soon-as-this-month.html\">CNBC</a>. &#34;The retail sectors where middle- and lower-income families spend money are likely to benefit some from this.&#34; </p><p>One parent told <a href=\"https://www.cnbc.com/2021/06/26/parents-anxiously-await-the-start-of-child-tax-credit-payments-.html\">CNBC</a> she&#39;s planning to use some of the money from the child tax credit on school supplies. Fresh EBT, an app to track food stamp balances, found users also plan to spend some of the payments on back-to-school items, as reported by <a href=\"https://www.nytimes.com/2021/07/12/us/politics/child-tax-credit-payments.html\">The New York Times</a>. </p><h2>People also stashed away savings over the last year</h2><p>According to Deloitte&#39;s back-to-school surveys, spending for both college and K-12 will be larger this year. Deloitte projects back-to-school spending for K-12 to increase by roughly 16% from the year before to $32.5 billion. Even as some students return to in-person learning, Deloitte found spending on tech will be 37% higher than in 2020. A survey from <a href=\"https://advisory.kpmg.us/articles/2021/consumer-pulse-survey-back-to-school-2021.html\">KPMG</a> and <a href=\"https://www.mastercard.com/news/press/2021/june/back-to-school-u-s-retail-sales-expected-to-grow-5-5-compared-to-last-year-according-to-mastercard-spendingpulse/\">Mastercard</a> also shows spending will be much higher this year than last year.</p><p>Rod Sides, vice chairman of Deloitte and Deloitte&#39;s US retail, wholesale, and distribution leader, told Insider he thinks one of the reasons consumers will be shopping earlier is because they want their kids to begin the school year with the items they need. </p><p>&#34;And there&#39;s more money available for that,&#34; Sides said. &#34;Generally when you&#39;ve got reasonably low unemployment and a high savings rate that usually translates to a much higher spending season.&#34;</p><p>The personal savings rate in May 2021 was <a href=\"https://www.bea.gov/news/2021/personal-income-and-outlays-may-2021\">12.4%</a>, higher than pre-pandemic rates. Personal savings totaled to <a href=\"https://www.bea.gov/news/2021/personal-income-and-outlays-may-2021\">$2.29 trillion</a> in May. The unemployment rate has fallen from pandemic highs and now stands at 5.9%, still higher than the pre-pandemic rate of 3.5%.</p><p>Additionally, a recent <a href=\"https://advisory.kpmg.us/articles/2021/consumer-pulse-survey-back-to-school-2021.html\">KPMG survey</a> of 1,000 people found that 39% of those who plan to spend more think items will be more expensive.</p><p>&#34;According to KPMG economic analysis, many products are seeing a spike in prices, driven by the combination of supply shocks to US manufacturing suppliers and strong demand for goods, including certain school shopping categories,&#34; KPMG <a href=\"https://advisory.kpmg.us/articles/2021/consumer-pulse-survey-back-to-school-2021.html\">wrote</a>.</p><div more common, demand for individually sold graphics cards has spiked dramatically, leaving most stores out of stock on a day-to-day basis. Just a few retailers, like <a href=\"https://www.microcenter.com/category/4294966937/graphics-cards\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Microcenter</a>, <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1746130097971015527\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Best Buy</a>, and <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.newegg.com%2FVideo-Cards-Video-Devices%2FCategory%2FID-38\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Newegg</a>, have advertised restocks. Manufacturer <a href=\"https://www.evga.com/products/productlist.aspx?type=0\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">EVGA</a> offers direct sales of the latest graphics cards, but the constant demand has created a lengthy waitlist for potential buyers.</p><p>International tariffs and resellers on eBay and Amazon have also led to graphics cards being sold way above their suggested retail price. That said, it&#39;s important to remember that stock remains hard to come by for all the models we&#39;ve listed, so prices above MSRP are likely unavoidable for the time being.</p><p>The starting prices we&#39;ve listed are for reference so you can decide whether any higher prices you may come across are worth the premium. We&#39;ll update this page with more buying options and restock alerts as they&#39;re announced.</p><h2>Nvidia RTX 30 series graphics cards</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60dc87d6a08b100012b4177f?format=jpeg\" alt=\"NVIDIA GeForce RTX 3060 Ti 8GB GDDR6 PCI Express 4.0 Graphics Card\" height=\"300\" width=\"600\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>Nvidia&#39;s RTX 3060ti graphics card.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Best Buy</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>Nvidia has described the demand for its latest series of <a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nvidia.com%2Fen-us%2Fgeforce%2Fgraphics-cards%2F30-series%2Feries%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">RTX 30 graphics cards</a> as &#34;unprecedented.&#34; Seven different cards have joined the RTX 30 line since September 2020, with recommended prices ranging from $329 to $1,500.</p><p>Priced at about $700, the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nvidia.com%2Fen-us%2Fgeforce%2Fgraphics-cards%2F30-series%2Frtx-3080-3080ti%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">RTX 3080</a> is an ideal choice for most people that will meet the needs of all but the most hardcore PC gaming enthusiasts. The $400 <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nvidia.com%2Fen-us%2Fgeforce%2Fgraphics-cards%2F30-series%2Frtx-3060-3060ti%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">RTX 3060 Ti</a> is a perfect pick for midrange and budget PCs, delivering excellent performance at 1080p, but struggling when pushed to 4K.</p><p>Nvidia graphics cards also have excellent software features and developer support that can benefit gamers who stream or record their gameplay for YouTube and Twitch. Nvidia&#39;s exclusive DLSS software helps improve performance in certain games by using artificial intelligence to upscale visuals.</p><table><tbody><tr><td><p><strong>Nvidia graphics sponsored\">RTX 3090</a></p></td><td><p>$1,500</p></td><td><p>4K/144hz</p></td></tr></tbody></table><h2><strong>AMD Radeon RX 6000 series g</strong>raphics cards</h2><figure>\n\t<img src=\"https://i.insider.com/60dc8959cad1220011caf338?format=jpeg\" alt=\"AMD RX 6800XT graphics cad\" height=\"565\" width=\"1131\" charset=\"\">\n<figcaption>The AMD RX 6800XT was released in November 2020.\n<p class=\"copyright\">AMD</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><p>AMD&#39;s graphics cards aren&#39;t quite as popular as Nvidia&#39;s, but they boast plenty of power and are generally less expensive than their RTX counterparts. AMD cards get an additional performance boost when paired with AMD processors, which compete with Intel as the most popular gaming CPUs, and are generally more cost effective.</p><p>At $649 <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1746130234476129236\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored nofollow sponsored\">AMD Radeon 6800XT</a> offers comparable performance to the RTX 3080 for $50 less, while the $579 <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1746130264230503250\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">AMD RX 6800</a> is a parallel to the $599 RTX 3070ti. The $999 <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1746130298352358207\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Radeon RX 6900XT</a> outperforms the $1,500 RTX 3090 in some games, but AMD&#39;s cards struggle with some newer features, like ray traced lighting and AI-powered resolution scaling. </p><p>Certain newly released games with those features will likely run slightly better on Nvidia hardware until AMD develops its own solutions to boost performance. On the other hand, some popular titles like &#34;<a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.gamestop.com%2Fvideo-games%2Fpc-gaming%2Fgames%2Fproducts%2Fborderlands-3%2F10175131.html%3Fcondition%3DDigital\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Borderlands 3</a>&#34; run better on AMD devices, so the performance differences will vary depending on your choice of games.</p><table><tbody><tr><td><p><strong>AMD graphics card</strong></p></td><td><p><strong>Starting price</strong></p></td><td><p><strong>Target resolution and refresh graphics card</h2><p>Recommended retailers for an Nvidia or AMD graphics card include <a href=\"https://www.microcenter.com/category/4294966937/graphics-cards\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Microcenter</a>, <a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1746130423038040601\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Best Buy</a>, <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.newegg.com%2FVideo-Cards-Video-Devices%2FCategory%2FID-38\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Newegg</a>, and Amazon (<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/stores/page/48855DAB-2174-4261-AB9F-6C25BC7BEF04?ingress=3&visitId=463edd48-62de-4e84-b9d1-80fdc17d7ce57ce5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Nvidia</a>, <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/stores/page/14A8C84F-E4B1-48CA-8502-E2CC2AC0D9EA?ingress=0&visitId=2abaa1c0-9f35-4b93-b771-b23a7862f816f816\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">AMD</a>). Unfortunately, inventory remains sold out at most store, but restocks occur from time to time. <a href=\"https://www.amd.com/en/where-to-buy/radeon-rx-6000-series-graphics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">AMD</a> also sell units from its own online store, and <a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nvidia.com%2Fen-us%2Fgeforce%2Fgraphics-cards%2F30-series%2Feries%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Nvidia</a> has a tool for checking stock at other retailers.</p><p>If you&#39;re on the hunt for an Nvidia or AMD graphics card we recommend checking these landing pages on a regular basis:</p><ul><li><a href=\"https://www.microcenter.com/category/4294966937/graphics-cards\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Microcenter</a></li><li><a href=\"https://shop-links.co/1746130423038040601\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Best Buy</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.newegg.com%2Fproduct-shuffle\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored nofollow sponsored\">Newegg</a> (new graphic cards are sold through a daily lotto due to low stock)</li><li>Amazon (<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/stores/page/48855DAB-2174-4261-AB9F-6C25BC7BEF04?ingress=3&visitId=463edd48-62de-4e84-b9d1-80fdc17d7ce57ce5\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Nvidia</a>, <a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/stores/page/14A8C84F-E4B1-48CA-8502-E2CC2AC0D9EA?ingress=0&visitId=2abaa1c0-9f35-4b93-b771-b23a7862f816f816\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">AMD</a>)</li><li><a href=\"https://go.skimresources.com?id=35871X943606&xs=1&url=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nvidia.com%2Fen-us%2Fgeforce%2Fgraphics-cards%2F30-series%2Feries%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">Nvidia</a></li><li><a href=\"https://www.amd.com/en/where-to-buy/radeon-rx-6000-series-graphics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">AMD</a></li></ul><p>Manufacturer <a href=\"https://www.evga.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">EVGA</a> is also offering a virtual waitlist via its website, so you can choose to be contacted by email when stock is available. However, the EVGA waitlist is months long, and the RTX 3080 and RTX 3060ti are in especially high demand.</p><h2>How to shop for a graphics card</h2><p>New graphics cards are incredibly hard to buy right now due to an international chip shortage that began in 2020. Resellers are charging far more than retail price on eBay and Amazon and even older cards are selling for above market rate. Given the current market situation it may be more affordable to shop for a pre-built gaming PC or laptop, rather than buying a graphics card separately and building your own.<br><br>Prices for the same cards can vary between manufacturers, with upgrades like extra cooling fans or RGB lighting increasing the cost. Graphics cards shipped were also impacted by a US tariff increase that arrived in early 2021, leading manufacturers to <a href=\"https://www.theverge.com/2021/1/13/22228470/nvidia-evga-zotac-raise-prices-rtx-3080-3070-3060-3090\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">increase their prices by $70 to $300</a> more than what RTX 30 series and AMD 6000 series cards originally sold for in fall 2020.</p><h2>What to know before buying a graphics card</h2><p>The graphics card might be the most important part of building a gaming PC, as it will likely determine your computer&#39;s peak performance. However, the more you spend on a graphics card, the more you&#39;ll need to spend on other parts to make sure you&#39;re not limiting its potential.</p><p>Even a $1,500 graphics card like the <a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/reviews/out?u=https%3A%2F%2Fwww.nvidia.com%2Fen-us%2Fgeforce%2Fgraphics-cards%2F30-series%2Frtx-3090%2F\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener sponsored\">RTX 3090</a> can struggle if paired with an old processor or motherboard, so be sure to make sure the components in your PC are all modern and compatible before spending most of your budget on a graphics card. </p><p>Specifically, you should make sure your power supply can deliver requirements for your card of choice, and you should see if your motherboard supports PCI 4.0. A weak CPU can create a bottleneck that limits the overall speed of your gaming computer too, so don&#39;t overspend on your graphics card if you can&#39;t upgrade your CPU to a similar quality.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a href='https://www.businessinsider.com/where-to-buy-graphics-card-nvidia-amd'>Business Insider</a></div><div strategists said.\n<p class=\"copyright\">Michael Gottschalk/Getty Images</p>\n</figcaption>\n</figure><ul class=\"summary-list\">\n<li>Wall Street firms are increasingly keen on European stocks, as many expect the rapid US rally to slow.</li>\n<li>Strategists say Europe&#39;s economy still has further to rebound and that its stocks are cheap.</li>\n<li>They also say the continent has plenty of cyclical stocks that do better when growth and inflation rise.</li>\n<li id=\"recirc\"><a href=\"https://newsletter.businessinsider.com/join/4np/10-things-opening-bell?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingest?utm_source=markets&utm_medium=ingestdium=ingest?utm_source=markets&#38;utm_medium=ingest\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><strong>Sign up here for our daily newsletter, 10 Things Before the Opening Bell</strong></a><strong>.</strong></li>\n</ul><p>Wall Street strategists have zeroed in on European stocks as the place to realize chunky gains in the coming year, as the red-hot rally in US equities cools.</p><p>Morgan Stanley, BlackRock, Nuveen and JPMorgan Asset Management are just some of the financial firms that have said Europe is the place to be for investors, given the economic recovery is picking up pace and the continent has more &#34;cyclical&#34; firms that stand to benefit from the rebound.</p><p>BlackRock has said it is now &#34;overweight&#34; on European stocks and &#34;neutral&#34; on the US, along with a number of other firms such as Morgan Stanley. And Tuesday&#39;s Bank of America survey found that fund managers increased their allocation to eurozone stocks in June, with more investors keen on the region than at any time since January 2018.</p><p><em><strong>Read more: </strong><a href=\"https://www.businessinsider.com/global-recovery-bets-top-themes-nuveen-stock-chief-saira-malik-2021-6\">Saira Malik manages $420 billion as the stock-investment chief for asset manager Nuveen, and her 3 strategies have all beaten the market over the past year. She told us 4 top themes traders could use to capitalize on the broadening global recovery.</a></em></p><p><strong>Strategists are cooling on US stocks after a breakneck rally</strong></p><p>The <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/s&p_500_500\">S&#38;P 500</a> has rocketed around 90% from its March 2020 lows, as huge amounts of monetary and fiscal stimulus, as well as increased interest from retail traders, have driven up stocks.</p><p>Many on Wall Street think the index has probably logged the bulk of its gains already, although they, by and large, think it should rise solidly from here. Analysts on average predict the S&#38;P 500 will <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/sp500-outlook-increase-record-high-reflation-trade-us-stocks-2021-7\">rise around 10%</a> over the next 12 months, compared to its more than 35% gain over the previous year, according to estimates compiled by data firm FactSet.</p><p><a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/news/stocks/stock-market-news-today-inflation-prices-cpi-sp500-dow-industrials-2021-7\">Strong inflation</a> and the potential for a rebound in bond yields are two worries for US investors, as they make stocks look less attractive. Potentially higher taxes and a natural slowdown in economic growth after the rebound over the first half of 2021 are two other concerns.</p><p><strong>European stocks could rise strongly as the rebound picks up speed</strong></p><p>At the heart of Wall Street&#39;s interest in European stocks is the fact that the rebound in the eurozone still has further to run compared to the US recovery.</p><p>&#34;The European economy is considerably earlier in its recovery than peers, which should ensure that growth momentum remains stronger for longer,&#34; Morgan Stanley analysts said in the bank&#39;s mid-year outlook.</p><p>Strong growth could act as a boon for the region&#39;s <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/index/stoxx_europe_600\">Stoxx 600</a> index, which has risen around 57% since its March 2020 low, compared to the S&#38;P 500&#39;s 90% increase.</p><p>The analysts added: &#34;European equities remain cheap and unloved in a global context with relative valuations close to long-term lows.&#34;</p><p>Strategists are also keen on Europe because it has more companies that are &#34;cyclical&#34; - that is, which stand to benefit from stronger growth and inflation. That compares favorably to the US, which has more &#34;growth&#34; stocks that fare well when inflation and bond yields are low like <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/tsla-stock\">Tesla</a> and <a href=\"https://markets.businessinsider.com/stocks/nflx-stock\">Netflix</a>.</p><p>BlackRock&#39;s strategists said in its recent mid-year outlook that cyclical sectors in Europe such as technology and financials &#34;could be well positioned to play catch up as the restart broadens beyond the US.&#34;</p><p>What&#39;s more, the European Union is set to launch a recovery fund in the second half of the year, Morgan Stanley said. It could release as much as $940 billion into economies over the next five years.</p><div class=\"read-original\">Read the original article on <a
